/>.es</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Canary Islands</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">\xc9\x99</span><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/\xc9\x9b\xc9\x99r/: &#39;are&#39; in &#39;bare&#39;">\xc9\x9b\xc9\x99r</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <i lang="es">Islas Canarias</i>, <small>pronounced&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[\xcb\x88islas ka\xcb\x88na\xc9\xbejas]</a></span>), also known informally as <i>the Canaries</i>, is a Spanish <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, in a region known as <a href="/wiki/Macaronesia" title="Macaronesia">Macaronesia</a>. At their closest point to the African mainland, they are 100 kilometres (62 miles) west of <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>. They are the southernmost of the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">autonomous communities of Spain</a>, and are located in the <a href="/wiki/African_Plate" title="African Plate">African Tectonic Plate</a>. The archipelago is economically and politically European, and is part of the <a href="/wiki/Special_Member_State_territories_and_the_European_Union#Outermost_regions" class="mw-redirect" title="Special Member State territories and the European Union">European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Utreta_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Utreta-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The eight main islands are (from largest to smallest in area) <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura" title="Fuerteventura">Fuerteventura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lanzarote" title="Lanzarote">Lanzarote</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Palma" title="La Palma">La Palma</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Gomera" title="La Gomera">La Gomera</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Hierro" title="El Hierro">El Hierro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Graciosa,_Canary_Islands" title="Graciosa, Canary Islands">La Graciosa</a>. The archipelago includes many smaller islands and islets, including <a href="/wiki/Alegranza" title="Alegranza">Alegranza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islote_de_Lobos" class="mw-redirect" title="Islote de Lobos">Isla de Lobos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monta%C3%B1a_Clara" title="Monta\xc3\xb1a Clara">Monta\xc3\xb1a Clara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roque_del_Oeste" title="Roque del Oeste">Roque del Oeste</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Roque_del_Este" title="Roque del Este">Roque del Este</a>. It also includes a number of rocks, including those of Salmor, Fasnia, Bonanza, <a href="/wiki/Roque_de_Garachico" title="Roque de Garachico">Garachico</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Roques_de_Anaga" title="Roques de Anaga">Anaga</a>. In ancient times, the island chain was often referred to as "the Fortunate Isles".<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The Canary Islands are the southernmost region of <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, and the largest and most populous archipelago of Macaronesia.<sup id="cite_ref-catalogo.museosdetenerife.org_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-catalogo.museosdetenerife.org-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Because of their location, the Canary Islands have historically been considered a bridge between the four continents of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2019, the Canary Islands had a population of 2,153,389<sup id="cite_ref-BOE_pop_2019_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOE_pop_2019-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> with a density of 287.39 inhabitants per km<sup>2</sup>, making it the eighth most populous autonomous community. The population is mostly concentrated in the two capital islands: around 43% on the island of <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a> and 40% on the island of <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a>.\n</p><p>The Canary Islands, especially Tenerife, Gran Canaria, Fuerteventura, and Lanzarote, are a major tourist destination, with over 12&#160;million visitors per year. This is due to their beaches, subtropical climate, and important natural attractions, especially <a href="/wiki/Maspalomas" title="Maspalomas">Maspalomas</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Teide_National_Park" title="Teide National Park">Teide National Park</a>, and Mount <a href="/wiki/Teide" title="Teide">Teide</a> (a World Heritage Site) in <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a>. Mount Teide is the third tallest volcano in the world, measured from its base on the ocean floor.<sup id="cite_ref-gobiernodecanarias1_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gobiernodecanarias1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-webtenerife1_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-webtenerife1-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Because of the islands\xe2\x80\x99 <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Subtropical climate">subtropical climate</a>, it has long, hot summers, and moderately warm winters.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The amount of precipitation and the level of maritime moderation vary depending on location and elevation. The archipelago includes green areas as well as desert areas. The islands\xe2\x80\x99 high mountains are ideal for astronomical observation, because they lie above the <a href="/wiki/Inversion_(meteorology)" title="Inversion (meteorology)">temperature inversion</a> layer. As a result, the archipelago boasts two professional observatories: <a href="/wiki/Teide_Observatory" title="Teide Observatory">Teide Observatory</a> on the island of Tenerife, and <a href="/wiki/Roque_de_los_Muchachos_Observatory" title="Roque de los Muchachos Observatory">Roque de los Muchachos Observatory</a> on the island of La Palma.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1927, the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Canary_Islands" title="Province of Canary Islands">Province of Canary Islands</a> was split into two provinces. In 1982, the autonomous community of the Canary Islands was established. The cities of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a> and <a href="/wiki/Las_Palmas_de_Gran_Canaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Palmas de Gran Canaria">Las Palmas de Gran Canaria</a> are, jointly, the capital of the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-es.wikisource.org_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-es.wikisource.org-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gobiernodecanarias.org_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gobiernodecanarias.org-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Those cities are also, respectively, the capitals of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_provinces" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish provinces">provinces</a> of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Santa Cruz de Tenerife (province)">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a> and <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Las_Palmas" title="Province of Las Palmas">Las Palmas</a>. Las Palmas de Gran Canaria has been the largest city in the Canaries since 1768, except for a brief period in the 1910s.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Between the <a href="/wiki/1833_territorial_division_of_Spain" title="1833 territorial division of Spain">1833 territorial division of Spain</a> and 1927, Santa Cruz de Tenerife was the sole capital of the Canary Islands. In 1927, it was ordered by decree that the capital of the Canary Islands would be shared between two cities, and this arrangement persists to the present day.<sup id="cite_ref-Real_Decreto_wikisource_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Real_Decreto_wikisource-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Real_Decreto_Canarias_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Real_Decreto_Canarias-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The third largest city in the Canary Islands is <a href="/wiki/San_Crist%C3%B3bal_de_La_Laguna" title="San Crist\xc3\xb3bal de La Laguna">San Crist\xc3\xb3bal de La Laguna</a> (a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>) on Tenerife.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> This city is also home to the <i>Consejo Consultivo de Canarias</i>, which is the supreme consultative body of the Canary Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the era of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>, the Canaries were the main stopover for <a href="/wiki/Spanish_treasure_fleet" title="Spanish treasure fleet">Spanish galleons</a> on their way to the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>, which sailed that far south in order to catch the prevailing northeasterly <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">trade winds</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" class="toclevel-2 tocsection-48"><a href="#Prehistoric_fauna"><span class="tocnumber">11.1</span> <span class="toctext">Prehistoric fauna</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-49"><a tocsection-55"><a href="#Notable_athletes"><span class="tocnumber">14.1</span> <span class="toctext">Notable athletes</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-56"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-57"><a href="#History_2"><span class="tocnumber">15.1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-58"><a href="#Geography"><span class="tocnumber">15.2</span> <span class="toctext">Geography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-59"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">15.3</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-60"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-61"><a href="#Informational_notes"><span class="tocnumber">16.1</span> <span class="toctext">Informational notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-62"><a href="#Citations"><span class="tocnumber">16.2</span> <span class="toctext">Citations</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-63"><a href="#References_2"><span class="tocnumber">17</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-64"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">18</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-65"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">19</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The name <i>Islas Canarias</i> is likely derived from the Latin name <i>Canariae Insulae</i>, meaning "Islands of the Dogs", a name that was evidently generalized from the ancient name of one of these islands, <i>Canaria</i> \xe2\x80\x93 presumably Gran Canaria. According to the historian <a href="/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder" title="Pliny the Elder">Pliny the Elder</a>, the island <i>Canaria</i> contained "vast multitudes of dogs of very large size".<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Alternatively, it is said that the original inhabitants of the island, <a href="/wiki/Guanches" title="Guanches">Guanches</a>, used to worship dogs, mummified them and generally treated them as holy animals.<sup id="cite_ref-10_facts_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10_facts-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (January 2020)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Some hypothesize that the Canary Islands\' dog-worship and the ancient Egyptian cult of the dog-headed god <a href="/wiki/Anubis" title="Anubis">Anubis</a> are closely connected.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other theories speculate that the name comes from the <a href="/wiki/Nukkari" title="Nukkari">Nukkari</a> Berber tribe living in the Moroccan Atlas, named in Roman sources as <i>Canarii</i>, though Pliny again mentions the relation of this term with dogs.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The connection to dogs is retained in their depiction on the islands\' coat-of-arms.\n</p><p>It is considered that the aborigines of Gran Canaria called themselves "Canarios".<sup id="cite_ref-:0_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> It is possible that after being conquered, this name was used in plural in Spanish, i.e., as to refer to all of the islands as the Canarii-as.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>What is certain is that the name of the islands does not derive from the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Canary" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantic Canary">canary bird</a>; rather, the birds are named after the islands.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_geography">Physical geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Physical geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_Canary_Islands.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Map_of_the_Canary_Islands.svg/440px-Map_of_the_Canary_Islands.svg.png" decoding="async" width="440" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Map_of_the_Canary_Islands.svg/660px-Map_of_the_Canary_Islands.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Map_of_the_Canary_Islands.svg/880px-Map_of_the_Canary_Islands.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="3152" data-file-height="1400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_Canary_Islands.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the Canary Islands</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hacha_grande_from_papagayo_pano.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Hacha_grande_from_papagayo_pano.jpg/440px-Hacha_grande_from_papagayo_pano.jpg" decoding="async" width="440" height="99" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Hacha_grande_from_papagayo_pano.jpg/660px-Hacha_grande_from_papagayo_pano.jpg 1.5x, class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hacha_grande_from_papagayo_pano.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hacha_Grande" title="Hacha Grande">Hacha Grande</a>, a mountain in the south of Lanzarote, viewed from the road to the Playa de Papagayo.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Grancanaria.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Grancanaria.jpg/440px-Grancanaria.jpg" decoding="async" width="440" height="89" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Grancanaria.jpg/660px-Grancanaria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Grancanaria.jpg/880px-Grancanaria.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7413" data-file-height="1500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Grancanaria.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Panoramic view of Gran Canaria, with <a href="/wiki/Roque_Nublo" title="Roque Nublo">Roque Nublo</a> at the left and Roque Bentayga at the center</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a> is the largest and most populous island of the archipelago. <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a>, with 865,070 inhabitants, is both the Canary Islands\' second most populous island, and the third most populous one in Spain after <a href="/wiki/Majorca" class="mw-redirect" title="Majorca">Majorca</a> and Tenerife. The island of <a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura" title="Fuerteventura">Fuerteventura</a> is the second largest in the archipelago and located 100&#160;km (62&#160;mi) from the African coast.\n</p><p>The islands form the <a href="/wiki/Macaronesia" title="Macaronesia">Macaronesia</a> <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madeira_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Madeira Islands">Madeira</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Savage_Isles" class="mw-redirect" title="Savage Isles">Savage Isles</a>. The Canary Islands is the largest and most populated archipelago of the Macaronesia region.<sup id="cite_ref-catalogo.museosdetenerife.org_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-catalogo.museosdetenerife.org-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The archipelago consists of seven large and several smaller islands, all of which are volcanic in origin.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The antipodes of the Canary Islands are found in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>, between <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">New Caledonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and the ocean.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to the position of the islands with respect to the north-east <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">trade winds</a>, the climate can be mild and wet or very dry. Several native species form <a href="/wiki/Laurisilva" class="mw-redirect" title="Laurisilva">laurisilva</a> forests.\n</p><p>As a consequence, the individual islands in the Canary archipelago tend to have distinct <a href="/wiki/Microclimate" title="Microclimate">microclimates</a>. Those islands such as <a href="/wiki/El_Hierro" title="El Hierro">El Hierro</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Palma" title="La Palma">La Palma</a> and <a href="/wiki/La_Gomera" title="La Gomera">La Gomera</a> lying to the west of the archipelago have a climate which is influenced by the moist <a href="/wiki/Canary_Current" title="Canary Current">Canary Current</a>. They are well vegetated even at low levels and have extensive tracts of sub-tropical laurisilva forest. As one travels east toward the African coast, the influence of the current diminishes, and the islands become increasingly arid. <a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura" title="Fuerteventura">Fuerteventura</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lanzarote" title="Lanzarote">Lanzarote</a>, the islands which are closest to the African mainland, are effectively desert or semi desert. <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a> is known as a "continent in miniature" for its diverse landscapes like <a href="/wiki/Maspalomas" title="Maspalomas">Maspalomas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roque_Nublo" title="Roque Nublo">Roque Nublo</a>. In terms of its climate <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a> is particularly interesting. The north of the island lies under the influence of the moist Atlantic winds and is well vegetated, while the south of the island around the tourist resorts of <a href="/wiki/Playa_de_las_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="Playa de las Americas">Playa de las Americas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Los_Cristianos" title="Los Cristianos">Los Cristianos</a> is arid. The island rises to almost 4,000&#160;m (13,000&#160;ft) above sea level, and at altitude, in the cool relatively wet climate, forests of the endemic pine <i><a href="/wiki/Pinus_canariensis" title="Pinus canariensis">Pinus canariensis</a></i> thrive. Many of the plant species in the Canary Islands, like the Canary Island pine and the <a href="/wiki/Dracaena_(plant)" title="Dracaena (plant)">dragon tree</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dracaena_draco" title="Dracaena draco">Dracaena draco</a></i> are endemic, as noted by <a href="/wiki/Sabin_Berthelot" title="Sabin Berthelot">Sabin Berthelot</a> and <a href="/wiki/Philip_Barker_Webb" class="mw-redirect" title="Philip Barker Webb">Philip Barker Webb</a> in their work, <i>L\'Histoire Naturelle des \xc3\x8eles Canaries</i> (1835\xe2\x80\x9350).<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The climate is <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Desert_climate" title="Desert climate">desertic</a>, moderated by the sea and in summer by the <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">trade winds</a>. There are a number of <a href="/wiki/Microclimate" title="Microclimate">microclimates</a> and the classifications range mainly from <a href="/wiki/Hot_semi-arid_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot semi-arid climate">semi-arid</a> to <a href="/wiki/Desert_climate" title="Desert climate">desert</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> the majority of the Canary Islands have a <a href="/wiki/Desert_climate" title="Desert climate">hot desert climate</a> represented as <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">BWh</a>, caused partly due to the cool <a href="/wiki/Canary_Current" title="Canary Current">Canary Current</a>. There also exists a subtropical humid climate which is very influenced by the ocean in the middle of the islands of <a href="/wiki/La_Gomera" title="La Gomera">La Gomera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a> and <a href="/wiki/La_Palma" title="La Palma">La Palma</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Laurisilva" class="mw-redirect" title="Laurisilva">laurisilva</a> forests grow.\n</p>\n<div>\n<table class="wikitable mw-collapsible" style="width:100%; text-align:center; line-height: 1.2em; margin:auto;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="14">Climate data for <a Meteorolog\xc3\xada</a><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="Geology of the Canary Islands">Geology of the Canary Islands</a></div>\n<p>The seven major islands, one minor island, and several small islets were originally volcanic islands, formed by the <a href="/wiki/Canary_hotspot" title="Canary hotspot">Canary hotspot</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The Canary Islands is the only place in Spain where <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_eruption" class="mw-redirect" title="Volcanic eruption">volcanic eruptions</a> have been recorded during the <a href="/wiki/Modern_Era" class="mw-redirect" title="Modern Era">Modern Era</a>, with some volcanoes still active (El Hierro, 2011).<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\nVolcanic islands such as those in the Canary chain often have steep ocean cliffs caused by catastrophic debris avalanches and <a href="/wiki/Landslide" title="Landslide">landslides</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Teide" title="Teide">Teide</a> <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcano</a> on Tenerife is the highest mountain in Spain, and the third tallest volcano on Earth on a volcanic ocean island. All the islands except La Gomera have been active in the last million years; four of them (Lanzarote, Tenerife, La Palma and El Hierro) have historical records of eruptions since European discovery. The islands rise from Jurassic <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_crust" title="Oceanic crust">oceanic crust</a> associated with the opening of the Atlantic. Underwater <a href="/wiki/Magmatism" title="Magmatism">magmatism</a> commenced during the Cretaceous, and continued to the present day. The current islands reached the ocean\'s surface during the <a href="/wiki/Miocene" title="Miocene">Miocene</a>. The islands were once considered as a distinct physiographic section of the <a href="/wiki/Atlas_Mountains" title="Atlas Mountains">Atlas Mountains</a> province, which in turn is part of the larger African Alpine System division, but are nowadays recognized as being related to a magmatic hot spot.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the summer of 2011 a series of low-magnitude earthquakes occurred beneath El Hierro. These had a linear trend of northeast\xe2\x80\x93southwest. In October a submarine eruption occurred about <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1020198016">.mw-parser-output .frac{white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output .frac .num,.mw-parser-output .frac .den{font-size:80%;line-height:0;vertical-align:super}.mw-parser-output .frac .den{vertical-align:sub}.mw-parser-output .sr-only{border:0;clip:rect(0,0,0,0);height:1px;margin:-1px;overflow:hidden;padding:0;position:absolute;width:1px}</style>2&#160;km (<span class="frac" role="math">1<span class="sr-only">+</span><span class="num">1</span>&#8260;<span class="den">4</span></span>&#160;mi) south of Restinga. This eruption produced gases and pumice, but no explosive activity was reported.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The following table shows the highest mountains in each of the islands:\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a Clara</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_symbols">Natural symbols</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Natural symbols">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_animal_and_plant_symbols_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="List of animal and plant symbols of the Canary Islands">List of animal and plant symbols of the Canary Islands</a></div>\n<p>The official natural symbols associated with Canary Islands are the bird <i><a href="/wiki/Serinus_canaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Serinus canaria">Serinus canaria</a></i> (canary) and the <i><a href="/wiki/Phoenix_canariensis" title="Phoenix canariensis">Phoenix canariensis</a></i> palm.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional center">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Serinus_canaria_LC0210.jpg/120px-Serinus_canaria_LC0210.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="86" class="gallerytext">\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/Serinus_canaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Serinus canaria">Serinus canaria</a></i>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Phoenix_canariensis_ag.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" id="National_parks">National parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: National parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Caldera_de_Taburiente_La_Palma.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Caldera_de_Taburiente_La_Palma.jpg/220px-Caldera_de_Taburiente_La_Palma.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Caldera_de_Taburiente_La_Palma.jpg/330px-Caldera_de_Taburiente_La_Palma.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Caldera_de_Taburiente_La_Palma.jpg/440px-Caldera_de_Taburiente_La_Palma.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Caldera_de_Taburiente_La_Palma.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Caldera_de_Taburiente_National_Park" title="Caldera de Taburiente National Park">Caldera de Taburiente National Park</a> (La Palma).</div></div></div>\n<p>Four of Spain\'s thirteen national parks are located in the Canary Islands, more than any other autonomous community. Two of these have been declared <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Sites" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Sites">World Heritage Sites</a> and the other two are part of <a href="/wiki/Biosphere_Reserves" class="mw-redirect" title="Biosphere Reserves">Biosphere Reserves</a>. The parks are:<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable">\n\n<tbody><tr align="left">\n<th class="unsortable">Park</th>\n<th class="unsortable">Island</th>\n<th>Area</th>\n<th>Year of Designation</th>\n<th class="unsortable">UNESCO Status\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Caldera_de_Taburiente_National_Park" title="Caldera de Taburiente National Park">Caldera de Taburiente National Park</a>\n</td>\n<td>La Palma\n</td>\n<td>46.9&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (18.1&#160;sq&#160;mi)\n</td>\n<td>1954\n</td>\n<td>Part of the La Palma Biosphere Reserve since 2002\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Garajonay_National_Park" title="Garajonay National Park">Garajonay National Park</a></td>\n<td>La Gomera\n</td>\n<td>39.86&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (15.39&#160;sq&#160;mi)\n</td>\n<td>1981\n</td>\n<td>World Heritage Site since 1986\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Teide_National_Park" title="Teide National Park">Teide National Park</a></td>\n<td>Tenerife\n</td>\n<td>18.99&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (7.33&#160;sq&#160;mi)\n</td>\n<td>1954\n</td>\n<td>World Heritage Site since 2007\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Timanfaya_National_Park" title="Timanfaya National Park">Timanfaya National Park</a></td>\n<td>Lanzarote\n</td>\n<td>51.07&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (19.72&#160;sq&#160;mi)\n</td>\n<td>1974\n</td>\n<td>Part of the Lanzarote Biosphere Reserve since 1993\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Teide_National_Park" title="Teide National Park">Teide National Park</a> is the oldest and largest national park in the Canary Islands and one of the oldest in Spain. Located in the geographic centre of the island of Tenerife, it is the most visited national park in Spain. In 2010, it became the most visited national park in Europe and second worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-diariodeavisos.com_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diariodeavisos.com-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sanborondon.info_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sanborondon.info-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The park\'s highlight is the <a href="/wiki/Teide" title="Teide">Teide</a> volcano; standing at an altitude of 3,715 metres (12,188&#160;ft),<sup id="cite_ref-IGN_PhysicalMap_2012_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IGN_PhysicalMap_2012-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> it is the highest elevation of the country and the third largest volcano on Earth from its base. In 2007, the Teide National Park was declared one of the <a href="/wiki/12_Treasures_of_Spain" title="12 Treasures of Spain">12 Treasures of Spain</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Spain_Canary_Islands_location_map_Province_of_Las_Palmas.svg" class="image"><img alt="" decoding="async" width="220" height="98" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1475" data-file-height="655" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Spain_Canary_Islands_location_map_Province_of_Las_Palmas.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Las_Palmas" title="Province of Las Palmas">Province of Las Palmas</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" 2x" data-file-width="1475" data-file-height="655" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Spain_Canary_Islands_location_map_Province_of_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Province of Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Province of Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Las_Palmas_-_Mapa_municipal.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Las_Palmas_-_Mapa_municipal.svg/220px-Las_Palmas_-_Mapa_municipal.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="117" class="thumbimage"
