//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Las_Palmas_-_Mapa_municipal.svg/440px-Las_Palmas_-_Mapa_municipal.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="778" data-file-height="413" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Las_Palmas_-_Mapa_municipal.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Municipalities in the Las Palmas Province</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_-_Mapa_municipal.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_-_Mapa_municipal.svg/220px-Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_-_Mapa_municipal.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="117" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_-_Mapa_municipal.svg/330px-Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_-_Mapa_municipal.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_-_Mapa_municipal.svg/440px-Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_-_Mapa_municipal.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="778" data-file-height="413" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_-_Mapa_municipal.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Municipalities in the Santa Cruz de Tenerife Province</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The regional executive body, the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="Parliament of the Canary Islands">Parliament of the Canary Islands</a>, is presided over by <a href="/wiki/%C3%81ngel_V%C3%ADctor_Torres" title="\xc3\x81ngel V\xc3\xadctor Torres">\xc3\x81ngel V\xc3\xadctor Torres</a> (<a href="/wiki/PSOE" class="mw-redirect" title="PSOE">PSOE</a>), the current <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="President of the Canary Islands">President of the Canary Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The latter is invested by the members of the regional legislature, the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="Parliament of the Canary Islands">Parliament of the Canary Islands</a>, that consists of 70 elected legislators. The <a href="/wiki/2019_Canarian_regional_election" title="2019 Canarian regional election">last regional election</a> took place in May 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The islands have 14 seats in the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Spain" title="Senate of Spain">Spanish Senate</a>. Of these, 11 seats are directly elected (3 for Gran Canaria, 3 for Tenerife, and 1 each for Lanzarote (including La Graciosa), Fuerteventura, La Palma, La Gomera and El Hierro) while the other 3 are appointed by the regional legislature.<sup id="cite_ref-compsenado_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-compsenado-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_geography">Political geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Political geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <b>Autonomous Community of the Canary Islands</b> consists of two <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Spain" title="Provinces of Spain">provinces</a> (<i>provincias</i>), <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Las_Palmas" title="Province of Las Palmas">Las Palmas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Province of Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a>, whose capitals (<a href="/wiki/Las_Palmas_de_Gran_Canaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Palmas de Gran Canaria">Las Palmas de Gran Canaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a>) are capitals of the autonomous community. Each of the seven major islands is ruled by an island council named <i>Cabildo Insular</i>. Each island is subdivided into smaller <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Spain" title="Municipalities of Spain">municipalities</a> (<i>municipios</i>); <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Las_Palmas" title="List of municipalities in Las Palmas">Las Palmas is divided into 34 municipalities</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="List of municipalities in Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife is divided into 54 municipalities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The international boundary of the Canaries is the subject of dispute between Spain and Morocco. Morocco\'s official position is that international laws regarding territorial limits do not authorise Spain to claim seabed boundaries based on the territory of the Canaries, since the Canary Islands enjoy a large degree of autonomy. In fact, the islands do not enjoy any special degree of autonomy as each one of the Spanish regions is considered an <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_community" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous community">autonomous community</a> with equal status to the European ones. <span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">Under the <a href="/wiki/Law_of_the_Sea" class="mw-redirect" title="Law of the Sea">Law of the Sea</a>, the only islands not granted territorial waters or an <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zone" title="Exclusive economic zone">exclusive economic zone</a> (EEZ) are those that are not fit for human habitation or do not have an economic life of their own, which is not the case of the Canary Islands.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The boundary determines the ownership of seabed oil deposits and other ocean resources. Morocco and Spain have been unable to agree on a compromise regarding the territorial boundary, since neither nation wants to cede its claimed right to the vast resources whose ownership depends upon the boundary. In 2002, for example, Morocco rejected a unilateral Spanish proposal.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canarian_nationalism">Canarian nationalism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Canarian nationalism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Canarian_nationalism" title="Canarian nationalism">Canarian nationalism</a></div>\n<p>There are some pro-independence political parties, like the <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_the_Canaries" title="National Congress of the Canaries">National Congress of the Canaries</a> (CNC) and the <a href="/wiki/Popular_Front_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="Popular Front of the Canary Islands">Popular Front of the Canary Islands</a>, but their popular support is almost insignificant, with no presence in either the autonomous parliament or the <i>cabildos insulares</i>.\n</p><p>According to a 2012 study by the <a href="/wiki/Centro_de_Investigaciones_Sociol%C3%B3gicas" title="Centro de Investigaciones Sociol\xc3\xb3gicas">Centro de Investigaciones Sociol\xc3\xb3gicas</a>, when asked about national identity, the majority of respondents from the Canary Islands (49.3%) consider themselves Spanish and Canarian in equal measures, followed by 37.1% who consider themselves more Canarian than Spanish. Only 6.1% of the respondents consider themselves only Canarian.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>National Sentiment in the Canary Islands<sup id="cite_ref-cis2956_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cis2956-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<td>Only Spanish</td>\n<td>3.5%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>More Spanish than Canarian</td>\n<td>2.0%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Equally Spanish and Canarian</td>\n<td>49.3%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>More Canarian than Spanish</td>\n<td>37.1%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Only Canarian</td>\n<td>6.1%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Did not answer</td>\n<td>2.0%\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_and_pre-colonial_times">Ancient and pre-colonial times</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Ancient and pre-colonial times">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands_in_pre-colonial_times" title="Canary Islands in pre-colonial times">Canary Islands in pre-colonial times</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MNH_-_Mumie_Frau_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/MNH_-_Mumie_Frau_1.jpg/220px-MNH_-_Mumie_Frau_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/MNH_-_Mumie_Frau_1.jpg/330px-MNH_-_Mumie_Frau_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/MNH_-_Mumie_Frau_1.jpg/440px-MNH_-_Mumie_Frau_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MNH_-_Mumie_Frau_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Guanche_mummies" title="Guanche mummies">Guanche mummy</a> of a woman (830&#160;AD). <a href="/wiki/Museo_de_la_Naturaleza_y_el_Hombre" class="mw-redirect" title="Museo de la Naturaleza y el Hombre">Museo de la Naturaleza y el Hombre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Before the arrival of humans, the Canaries were inhabited by prehistoric animals; for example, the giant lizard (<i><a href="/wiki/Gallotia_goliath" title="Gallotia goliath">Gallotia goliath</a></i>), the <a href="/wiki/Tenerife_giant_rat" title="Tenerife giant rat">Tenerife</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria_giant_rat" title="Gran Canaria giant rat">Gran Canaria giant rats</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> and giant prehistoric tortoises, <i><a href="/wiki/Geochelone_burchardi" class="mw-redirect" title="Geochelone burchardi">Geochelone burchardi</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Geochelone_vulcanica" class="mw-redirect" title="Geochelone vulcanica">Geochelone vulcanica</a></i>.\n</p><p>The islands may have been visited by the <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenicians</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Carthage" title="Ancient Carthage">Carthaginians</a>. King <a href="/wiki/Juba_II" title="Juba II">Juba II</a>, Caesar <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">Augustus</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Numidia" title="Numidia">Numidian</a> prot\xc3\xa9g\xc3\xa9, is credited with discovering the islands for the Western world. According to <a href="/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder" title="Pliny the Elder">Pliny the Elder</a>, Juba found the islands uninhabited, but found "a small temple of stone" and "some traces of buildings".<sup id="cite_ref-Pliny_the_Elder_(77-79_AD)_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pliny_the_Elder_(77-79_AD)-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Juba dispatched a naval contingent to re-open the dye production facility at <a href="/wiki/Essaouira" title="Essaouira">Mogador</a> in what is now western Morocco in the early first century&#160;<a href="/wiki/AD" class="mw-redirect" title="AD">AD</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> That same naval force was subsequently sent on an exploration of the Canary Islands, using Mogador as their mission base.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The names given by Romans to the individual islands were <i>Ninguaria</i> or <i>Nivaria</i> (Tenerife), <i>Canaria</i> (Gran Canaria), <i>Pluvialia</i> or <i>Invale</i> (Lanzarote), <i>Ombrion</i> (La Palma), <i>Planasia</i> (Fuerteventura), <i>Iunonia</i> or <i>Junonia</i> (El Hierro) and <i>Capraria</i> (La Gomera).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pueblochico_guanches_A.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Pueblochico_guanches_A.jpg/220px-Pueblochico_guanches_A.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Pueblochico_guanches_A.jpg/330px-Pueblochico_guanches_A.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Pueblochico_guanches_A.jpg/440px-Pueblochico_guanches_A.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pueblochico_guanches_A.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Reconstruction of a <a href="/wiki/Guanches" title="Guanches">Guanche</a> settlement of Tenerife</div></div></div>\n<p>When the Europeans began to explore the islands in the late Middle Ages, they encountered several <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous peoples</a> living at a <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> level of technology. Although the prehistory of the settlement of the Canary Islands is still unclear, linguistic and genetic analyses seem to indicate that at least some of these inhabitants shared a common origin with the <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">Berbers</a> on the nearby North African coast.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The precolonial inhabitants came to be known collectively as the <a href="/wiki/Guanches" title="Guanches">Guanches</a>, although <i>Guanches</i> had been the name for only the indigenous inhabitants of Tenerife.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> From the 14th&#160;century onward, numerous visits were made by sailors from <a href="/wiki/Majorca" class="mw-redirect" title="Majorca">Majorca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a>. <a href="/wiki/Lancelotto_Malocello" title="Lancelotto Malocello">Lancelotto Malocello</a> settled on Lanzarote in 1312. The Majorcans established a <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">mission</a> with a bishop in the islands that lasted from 1350 to 1400.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Castilian_conquest">Castilian conquest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Castilian conquest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="Conquest of the Canary Islands">Conquest of the Canary Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="Kingdom of the Canary Islands">Kingdom of the Canary Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Crown of Castile</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Kingdom of Portugal</a></div>\n<p>In 1402, the Castilian conquest of the islands began, with the expedition of the French explorers <a href="/wiki/Jean_de_B%C3%A9thencourt" title="Jean de B\xc3\xa9thencourt">Jean de B\xc3\xa9thencourt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gadifer_de_la_Salle" title="Gadifer de la Salle">Gadifer de la Salle</a>, nobles and <a href="/wiki/Vassal" title="Vassal">vassals</a> of <a href="/wiki/Henry_III_of_Castile" title="Henry III of Castile">Henry III of Castile</a>, to Lanzarote. From there, they went on to conquer Fuerteventura (1405) and El Hierro. B\xc3\xa9thencourt received the title King of the Canary Islands, but still recognised King Henry III as his overlord.  It was not a simple military enterprise, given the aboriginal resistance on some islands. Neither was it politically, since the particular interests of the nobility (determined to strengthen their economic and political power through the acquisition of the islands) conflicted with those of the states, particularly Castile, which were in the midst of territorial expansion and in a process of strengthening of the Crown against the nobility.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AlonsoFernandezdeLugo2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/AlonsoFernandezdeLugo2.JPG/280px-AlonsoFernandezdeLugo2.JPG" decoding="async" width="280" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/AlonsoFernandezdeLugo2.JPG/420px-AlonsoFernandezdeLugo2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8d/AlonsoFernandezdeLugo2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="557" data-file-height="361" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AlonsoFernandezdeLugo2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Alonso_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Lugo" title="Alonso Fern\xc3\xa1ndez de Lugo">Alonso Fern\xc3\xa1ndez de Lugo</a> presenting the captured native Guanche kings of <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Monarchs" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic Monarchs">Catholic Monarchs</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Historians distinguish two periods in the conquest of the Canary Islands:\n</p><p>Aristocratic conquest (<i>Conquista se\xc3\xb1orial</i>). This refers to the early conquests carried out by the nobility, for their own benefit and without the direct participation of the Crown of Castile, which merely granted rights of conquest in exchange for pacts of vassalage between the noble conqueror and the Crown. One can identify within this period an early phase known as the Betancurian or Norman Conquest, carried out by <a href="/wiki/Jean_de_Bethencourt" class="mw-redirect" title="Jean de Bethencourt">Jean de Bethencourt</a> (who was originally from Normandy) and <a href="/wiki/Gadifer_de_la_Salle" title="Gadifer de la Salle">Gadifer de la Salle</a> between 1402 and 1405, which involved the islands of <a href="/wiki/Lanzarote" title="Lanzarote">Lanzarote</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Hierro" title="El Hierro">El Hierro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura" title="Fuerteventura">Fuerteventura</a>. The subsequent phase is known as the Castilian Conquest, carried out by Castilian nobles who acquired, through purchases, assignments and marriages, the previously conquered islands and also incorporated the island of <a href="/wiki/La_Gomera" title="La Gomera">La Gomera</a> around 1450.\n</p><p>Royal conquest (<i>Conquista realenga</i>). This defines the conquest between 1478 and 1496, carried out directly by the Crown of Castile, during the reign of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Monarchs" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic Monarchs">Catholic Monarchs</a>, who armed and partly financed the conquest of those islands which were still unconquered: <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Palma" title="La Palma">La Palma</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a>. This phase of the conquest came to an end in the year 1496, with the dominion of the island of Tenerife, bringing the entire Canarian Archipelago under the control of the Crown of Castile.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Columbus_House-Vegueta-Las_Palmas_Gran_Canaria.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Columbus_House-Vegueta-Las_Palmas_Gran_Canaria.jpg/220px-Columbus_House-Vegueta-Las_Palmas_Gran_Canaria.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Columbus_House-Vegueta-Las_Palmas_Gran_Canaria.jpg/330px-Columbus_House-Vegueta-Las_Palmas_Gran_Canaria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Columbus_House-Vegueta-Las_Palmas_Gran_Canaria.jpg/440px-Columbus_House-Vegueta-Las_Palmas_Gran_Canaria.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Columbus_House-Vegueta-Las_Palmas_Gran_Canaria.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Casa de Col\xc3\xb3n (Las Palmas de Gran Canaria), which Christopher Columbus visited during his first trip.</div></div></div>\n<p>B\xc3\xa9thencourt also established a base on the island of La Gomera, but it would be many years before the island was fully conquered. The natives of La Gomera, and of Gran Canaria, Tenerife, and La Palma, resisted the Castilian invaders for almost a century. In 1448 Maciot de B\xc3\xa9thencourt sold the lordship of Lanzarote to Portugal\'s Prince <a href="/wiki/Henry_the_Navigator" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry the Navigator">Henry the Navigator</a>, an action that was accepted by neither the natives nor the Castilians. Despite <a href="/wiki/Pope_Nicholas_V#cite_ref-8" title="Pope Nicholas V">Pope Nicholas V</a> ruling that the Canary Islands were under Portuguese control, the crisis swelled to a revolt which lasted until 1459 with the final expulsion of the Portuguese. In 1479, Portugal and Castile signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Alc%C3%A1%C3%A7ovas" title="Treaty of Alc\xc3\xa1\xc3\xa7ovas">Treaty of Alc\xc3\xa1\xc3\xa7ovas</a>, which settled disputes between Castile and Portugal over the control of the Atlantic. This treaty recognized Castilian control of the Canary Islands but also confirmed Portuguese possession of the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde islands</a>, and gave the Portuguese rights to any further islands or lands in the Atlantic that might be discovered.\n</p><p>The Castilians continued to dominate the islands, but due to the topography and the resistance of the native Guanches, they did not achieve complete control until 1496, when Tenerife and La Palma were finally subdued by <a href="/wiki/Alonso_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Lugo" title="Alonso Fern\xc3\xa1ndez de Lugo">Alonso Fern\xc3\xa1ndez de Lugo</a>. After that, the Canaries were incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Castile" title="Kingdom of Castile">Kingdom of Castile</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="After_the_conquest">After the conquest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: After the conquest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Canary_Islands_map_by_William_Dampier_1699_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15675.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Canary_Islands_map_by_William_Dampier_1699_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15675.jpg/170px-Canary_Islands_map_by_William_Dampier_1699_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15675.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="249" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Canary_Islands_map_by_William_Dampier_1699_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15675.jpg/255px-Canary_Islands_map_by_William_Dampier_1699_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15675.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Canary_Islands_map_by_William_Dampier_1699_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15675.jpg/340px-Canary_Islands_map_by_William_Dampier_1699_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15675.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="732" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Canary_Islands_map_by_William_Dampier_1699_-_Project_Gutenberg_eText_15675.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Maps of the Canary Islands drawn by <a href="/wiki/William_Dampier" title="William Dampier">William Dampier</a> during his voyage to <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">New Holland</a> in 1699.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Realm_of_Canary_Islands.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Realm_of_Canary_Islands.svg/170px-Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Realm_of_Canary_Islands.svg.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="239" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Realm_of_Canary_Islands.svg/255px-Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Realm_of_Canary_Islands.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Realm_of_Canary_Islands.svg/340px-Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Realm_of_Canary_Islands.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="874" data-file-height="1228" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Realm_of_Canary_Islands.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coat of arms of the Castilian and Spanish Realm of Canary Islands</div></div></div>\n<p>After the conquest, the Castilians imposed a new economic model, based on single-crop cultivation: first <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a>; then wine, an important item of trade with <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">England</a>. In this era, the first institutions of colonial government were founded. Gran Canaria, a colony of the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Crown of Castile</a> since 6 March 1480 (from 1556, of Spain), and Tenerife, a Spanish colony since 1496, each had its own governor. There has been speculation that the abundance of <a href="/wiki/Roccella_tinctoria" title="Roccella tinctoria">roccella tinctoria</a> on the Canary Islands offered a profit motive for <a href="/wiki/Jean_de_B%C3%A9thencourt" title="Jean de B\xc3\xa9thencourt">Jean de B\xc3\xa9thencourt</a> during his conquest of the islands. Lichen has been used for centuries to make dyes. This includes royal purple colors derived from roccella tinctoria, also known as orseille.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The cities of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a> and <a href="/wiki/Las_Palmas_de_Gran_Canaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Palmas de Gran Canaria">Las Palmas de Gran Canaria</a> became a stopping point for the Spanish <a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">conquistadors</a>, traders, and missionaries on their way to the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>. This trade route brought great prosperity to some of the social sectors of the islands. The islands became quite wealthy and soon were attracting merchants and adventurers from all over Europe. Magnificent palaces and churches were built on La Palma during this busy, prosperous period. The Church of El Salvador survives as one of the island\'s finest examples of the architecture of the 16th century. Civilian architecture survives in forms such as <a href="/wiki/Casas_de_los_S%C3%A1nchez-Ochando" title="Casas de los S\xc3\xa1nchez-Ochando">Casas de los S\xc3\xa1nchez-Ochando</a> or <a href="/wiki/Casa_Quintana" title="Casa Quintana">Casa Quintana</a>.\n</p><p>The Canaries\' wealth invited attacks by <a href="/wiki/Pirate" class="mw-redirect" title="Pirate">pirates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Privateer" title="Privateer">privateers</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turkish</a> <a href="/wiki/Admiral" title="Admiral">admiral</a> and privateer <a href="/wiki/Kemal_Reis" title="Kemal Reis">Kemal Reis</a> ventured into the Canaries in 1501, while <a href="/wiki/Murat_Reis_the_Elder" title="Murat Reis the Elder">Murat Reis the Elder</a> captured Lanzarote in 1585.\n</p><p>The most severe attack took place in 1599, during the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Revolt" title="Dutch Revolt">Dutch Revolt</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> fleet of 74 ships and 12,000 men, commanded by <a href="/wiki/Pieter_van_der_Does" title="Pieter van der Does">Pieter van der Does</a>, attacked the capital Las Palmas de Gran Canaria (the city had 3,500 of Gran Canaria\'s 8,545 inhabitants). The Dutch attacked the Castillo de la Luz, which guarded the harbor. The Canarians evacuated civilians from the city, and the Castillo surrendered (but not the city). The Dutch moved inland, but Canarian cavalry drove them back to Tamaraceite, near the city.\n</p><p>The Dutch then laid siege to the city, demanding the surrender of all its wealth. They received 12 sheep and 3 calves. Furious, the Dutch sent 4,000 soldiers to attack the Council of the Canaries, who were sheltering in the village of Santa Br\xc3\xadgida. 300 Canarian soldiers ambushed the Dutch in the village of Monte Lentiscal, killing 150 and forcing the rest to retreat. The Dutch concentrated on Las Palmas de Gran Canaria, attempting to burn it down. The Dutch pillaged <a href="/wiki/Maspalomas" title="Maspalomas">Maspalomas</a>, on the southern coast of Gran Canaria, <a href="/wiki/San_Sebasti%C3%A1n_de_La_Gomera" title="San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n de La Gomera">San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n</a> on La Gomera, and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_La_Palma" title="Santa Cruz de La Palma">Santa Cruz</a> on La Palma, but eventually gave up the siege of Las Palmas and withdrew.\n</p><p>In 1618 the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_pirates" title="Barbary pirates">Barbary pirates</a> attacked Lanzarote and La Gomera taking 1000 captives to be sold as <a href="/wiki/Barbary_slave_trade" title="Barbary slave trade">slaves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Another noteworthy attack occurred in 1797, when <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_(1797)" title="Battle of Santa Cruz de Tenerife (1797)">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a> was attacked by a British fleet under <a href="/wiki/Horatio_Nelson,_1st_Viscount_Nelson" title="Horatio Nelson, 1st Viscount Nelson">Horatio Nelson</a> on 25 July. The British were repulsed, losing almost 400 men. It was during this battle that Nelson lost his right arm.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="18th_to_19th_century">18th to 19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 18th to 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amaro_Pargo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Amaro_Pargo.jpg/220px-Amaro_Pargo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="209" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Amaro_Pargo.jpg/330px-Amaro_Pargo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Amaro_Pargo.jpg/440px-Amaro_Pargo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="854" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amaro_Pargo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Amaro_Pargo" title="Amaro Pargo">Amaro Pargo</a> (1678\xe2\x80\x931741), <a href="/wiki/Piracy" title="Piracy">corsair</a> and <a href="/wiki/Merchant" title="Merchant">merchant</a> from Tenerife who participated in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_treasure_fleet" title="Spanish treasure fleet">Spanish treasure fleet</a> (the Spanish-American trade route).</div></div></div>\n<p>The sugar-based economy of the islands faced stiff competition from Spain\'s <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> colonies. Low sugar prices in the 19th century caused severe recessions on the islands. A new cash crop, <a href="/wiki/Cochineal" title="Cochineal">cochineal</a> (<i>cochinilla</i>), came into cultivation during this time, reinvigorating the islands\' economy. During this time the Canarian-American trade was developed, in which Canarian products such as cochineal, sugarcane and rum were sold in American ports such as <a href="/wiki/Veracruz" title="Veracruz">Veracruz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Campeche" title="Campeche">Campeche</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Guaira" title="La Guaira">La Guaira</a> and <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the end of the 18th century, Canary Islanders had already emigrated to Spanish American territories, such as <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Veracruz" title="Veracruz">Veracruz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/San_Antonio,_Texas" class="mw-redirect" title="San Antonio, Texas">San Antonio, Texas</a><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/St._Bernard_Parish,_Louisiana" title="St. Bernard Parish, Louisiana">St. Bernard Parish, Louisiana</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> These economic difficulties spurred mass emigration during the 19th and first half of the 20th century, primarily to the Americas. Between 1840 and 1890 as many as 40,000 Canary Islanders emigrated to <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>. Also, thousands of Canarians moved to <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> where the Spanish monarchy felt that Canarians would adapt to island life better than other immigrants from the mainland of Spain. Deeply entrenched traditions, such as the Mascaras Festival in the town of <a href="/wiki/Hatillo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Hatillo, Puerto Rico">Hatillo, Puerto Rico</a>, are an example of Canarian culture still preserved in Puerto Rico. Similarly, many thousands of Canarians emigrated to the shores of <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War">Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War</a> of 1898, the Spanish fortified the islands against a possible American attack, but no such event took place.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romantic_period_and_scientific_expeditions">Romantic period and scientific expeditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Romantic period and scientific expeditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Coast_El_Golfo.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Coast_El_Golfo.JPG/220px-Coast_El_Golfo.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Coast_El_Golfo.JPG/330px-Coast_El_Golfo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Coast_El_Golfo.JPG/440px-Coast_El_Golfo.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2496" data-file-height="1664" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Coast_El_Golfo.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coast El Golfo, El Hierro</div></div></div>\n<p>Sirera and Renn (2004)<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> distinguish two different types of expeditions, or voyages, during the period 1770\xe2\x80\x931830, which they term "the Romantic period":\n</p><p>First are "expeditions financed by the States, closely related with the official scientific Institutions. characterised by having strict scientific objectives (and inspired by) the spirit of Illustration and progress". In this type of expedition, Sirera and Renn include the following travellers:\n</p>\n<ul><li>J. Edens, whose 1715 ascent and observations of Mt. Teide influenced many subsequent expeditions.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Louis_Feuill%C3%A9e" title="Louis Feuill\xc3\xa9e">Louis Feuill\xc3\xa9e</a> (1724), who was sent to measure the meridian of El Hierro and to map the islands.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jean-Charles_de_Borda" title="Jean-Charles de Borda">Jean-Charles de Borda</a> (1771, 1776) who more accurately measured the longitudes of the islands and the height of Mount Teide</li>\n<li>the <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Baudin" title="Nicolas Baudin">Baudin</a>-Ledru expedition (1796) which aimed to recover a valuable collection of natural history objects.</li></ul>\n<p>The second type of expedition identified by Sirera and Renn is one that took place starting from more or less private initiatives. Among these, the key exponents were the following:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt" title="Alexander von Humboldt">Alexander von Humboldt</a> (1799)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Christian_Leopold_von_Buch" title="Christian Leopold von Buch">Buch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christen_Smith_(botanist)" class="mw-redirect" title="Christen Smith (botanist)">Smith</a> (1815)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Broussonet" class="mw-redirect" title="Broussonet">Broussonet</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Philip_Barker_Webb" class="mw-redirect" title="Philip Barker Webb">Webb</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sabin_Berthelot" title="Sabin Berthelot">Sabin Berthelot</a>.</li></ul>\n<p>Sirera and Renn identify the period 1770\xe2\x80\x931830 as one in which "In a panorama dominated until that moment by France and England enters with strength and brio Germany of the Romantic period whose presence in the islands will increase".\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_20th_century">Early 20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Early 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bahia_luz_las_palmas_1912_jordao_da_luz_perestello.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Bahia_luz_las_palmas_1912_jordao_da_luz_perestello.jpg/220px-Bahia_luz_las_palmas_1912_jordao_da_luz_perestello.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Bahia_luz_las_palmas_1912_jordao_da_luz_perestello.jpg/330px-Bahia_luz_las_palmas_1912_jordao_da_luz_perestello.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Bahia_luz_las_palmas_1912_jordao_da_luz_perestello.jpg/440px-Bahia_luz_las_palmas_1912_jordao_da_luz_perestello.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="369" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bahia_luz_las_palmas_1912_jordao_da_luz_perestello.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Las_Palmas" title="Port of Las Palmas">port of Las Palmas</a> in 1912.</div></div></div>\n<p>At the beginning of the 20th century, the British introduced a new <a href="/wiki/Cash-crop" class="mw-redirect" title="Cash-crop">cash-crop</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">banana</a>, the export of which was controlled by companies such as <a href="/wiki/Fyffes" title="Fyffes">Fyffes</a>.\n</p><p>30 November 1833 the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Canary_Islands" title="Province of Canary Islands">Province of Canary Islands</a> had been created with the capital being declared as Santa Cruz de Tenerife.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The rivalry between the cities of Las Palmas de Gran Canaria and Santa Cruz de Tenerife for the capital of the islands led to the division of the <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> into two provinces on 23 September 1927.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the time of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Spanish_Republic" title="Second Spanish Republic">Second Spanish Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marxist" class="mw-redirect" title="Marxist">Marxist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anarchist" class="mw-redirect" title="Anarchist">anarchist</a> workers\' movements began to develop, led by figures such as Jose Miguel Perez and <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_Ascanio" title="Guillermo Ascanio">Guillermo Ascanio</a>. However, outside of a few municipalities, these organisations were a minority and fell easily to Nationalist forces during the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Franco_regime">Franco regime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Franco regime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Francoist_Spain" title="Francoist Spain">Francoist Spain</a></div>\n<p>In 1936, <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a> was appointed General Commandant of the Canaries. He joined the military revolt of 17 July which began the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>. Franco quickly took control of the archipelago, except for a few points of resistance on La Palma and in the town of <a href="/wiki/Vallehermoso,_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Vallehermoso, Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Vallehermoso</a>, on La Gomera. Though there was never a war in the islands, the post-war suppression of political dissent on the Canaries was most severe.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the Second World War, <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> prepared plans for the British seizure of the Canary Islands as a <a href="/wiki/Naval_base" title="Naval base">naval base</a>, in the event of <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> being invaded from the Spanish mainland.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;n. 1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Opposition to Franco\'s regime did not begin to organise until the late 1950s, which experienced an upheaval of parties such as the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Spain_(main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist Party of Spain (main)">Communist Party of Spain</a> and the formation of various nationalist, leftist parties.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Self-governance">Self-governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Self-governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Auditorio_de_Tenerife_Pano.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Auditorio_de_Tenerife_Pano.jpg/220px-Auditorio_de_Tenerife_Pano.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="105" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Auditorio_de_Tenerife_Pano.jpg/330px-Auditorio_de_Tenerife_Pano.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Auditorio_de_Tenerife_Pano.jpg/440px-Auditorio_de_Tenerife_Pano.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5692" data-file-height="2716" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Auditorio_de_Tenerife_Pano.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Auditorio_de_Tenerife" title="Auditorio de Tenerife">Auditorio de Tenerife</a> by <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Calatrava" title="Santiago Calatrava">Santiago Calatrava</a>, and an icon of contemporary architecture in the Canary Islands, (<a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a>)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/440px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" decoding="async" width="440" height="271" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/660px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/880px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 2x" data-file-width="2206" data-file-height="1358" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the European Union in the world with <a href="/wiki/Special_member_state_territories_and_the_European_Union" title="Special member state territories and the European Union">overseas countries and territories and outermost regions</a></div></div></div>\n<p>After the death of Franco, there was a pro-independence armed movement based in <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands_Independence_Movement" title="Canary Islands Independence Movement">Movement for the Independence and Self-determination of the Canaries Archipelago</a> (MAIAC). In 1968, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_African_Unity" title="Organisation of African Unity">Organisation of African Unity</a> recognized the MAIAC as a legitimate <a href="/wiki/African_independence_movements" title="African independence movements">African independence movement</a>, and declared the Canary Islands as an African territory still under foreign rule.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the establishment of a democratic <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> in Spain, <a href="/wiki/Self-governance" title="Self-governance">autonomy</a> was granted to the Canaries via a law passed in 1982, with a newly established autonomous devolved government and parliament. In 1983, the first autonomous elections were held. The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Spanish Socialist Workers&#39; Party">Spanish Socialist Workers\' Party</a> (PSOE) won. In the 2007 elections, the PSOE gained a plurality of seats, but the nationalist <a href="/wiki/Canarian_Coalition" title="Canarian Coalition">Canarian Coalition</a> and the conservative <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People&#39;s Party (Spain)">Partido Popular</a> (PP) formed a ruling coalition government.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Capitals">Capitals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Capitals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>At present, the Canary Islands is the only autonomous community in Spain that has two capitals: <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a> and <a href="/wiki/Las_Palmas_de_Gran_Canaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Palmas de Gran Canaria">Las Palmas de Gran Canaria</a>, since the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Statute_of_Autonomy_of_the_Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Statute of Autonomy of the Canary Islands (page does not exist)">Statute of Autonomy of the Canary Islands</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estatuto_de_Autonom%C3%ADa_de_Canarias" class="extiw" title="es:Estatuto de Autonom\xc3\xada de Canarias">es</a>&#93;</span> was created in 1982.<sup id="cite_ref-es.wikisource.org_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-es.wikisource.org-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gobiernodecanarias.org_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gobiernodecanarias.org-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The political capital of the archipelago did not exist as such until the nineteenth century. The first cities founded by the <a href="/wiki/Europeans" class="mw-redirect" title="Europeans">Europeans</a> at the time of the conquest of the Canary Islands in the 15th century were: <a href="/wiki/Telde" title="Telde">Telde</a> (in <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a>), <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Marcial_del_Rubic%C3%B3n&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="San Marcial del Rubic\xc3\xb3n (page does not exist)">San Marcial del Rubic\xc3\xb3n</a> (in <a href="/wiki/Lanzarote" title="Lanzarote">Lanzarote</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Betancuria" title="Betancuria">Betancuria</a> (in <a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura" title="Fuerteventura">Fuerteventura</a>). These cities boasted the first European institutions present in the archipelago, including <a href="/wiki/Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic">Catholic</a> <a href="/wiki/Bishoprics" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishoprics">bishoprics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Although, because the period of splendor of these cities developed before the total conquest of the archipelago and its incorporation into the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Crown of Castile</a> never had a political and real control of the entire Canary archipelago.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Las_Palmas_panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Las_Palmas_panorama.jpg/280px-Las_Palmas_panorama.jpg" decoding="async" width="280" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Las_Palmas_panorama.jpg/420px-Las_Palmas_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Las_Palmas_panorama.jpg/560px-Las_Palmas_panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3564" data-file-height="1476" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Las_Palmas_panorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Overview of Las Palmas de Gran Canaria.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vista_de_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Vista_de_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.png/280px-Vista_de_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.png" decoding="async" width="280" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Vista_de_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.png/420px-Vista_de_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Vista_de_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.png/560px-Vista_de_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.png 2x" data-file-width="4224" data-file-height="2376" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vista_de_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of Santa Cruz de Tenerife.</div></div></div>\n<p>The function of a Canarian city with full jurisdiction for the entire archipelago only exists after the conquest of the Canary Islands, although originally <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i>, that is, without legal and real meaning and linked to the headquarters of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands_General_Captaincy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Canary Islands General Captaincy (page does not exist)">Canary Islands General Captaincy</a>.\n</p><p>Las Palmas de Gran Canaria was the first city that exercised this function. This is because the residence of the Captain General of the Canary Islands was in this city during part of the sixteenth and seventeenth centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-junta_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-junta-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> In May 1661, the Captain General of the Canary Islands, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jer%C3%B3nimo_de_Benavente_y_Qui%C3%B1ones&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jer\xc3\xb3nimo de Benavente y Qui\xc3\xb1ones (page does not exist)">Jer\xc3\xb3nimo de Benavente y Qui\xc3\xb1ones</a>, moved the headquarters of the captaincy to the city of <a href="/wiki/San_Crist%C3%B3bal_de_La_Laguna" title="San Crist\xc3\xb3bal de La Laguna">San Crist\xc3\xb3bal de La Laguna</a> on the island of <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-portalcultura.mde_1_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-portalcultura.mde_1-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> This was due to the fact that this island since the conquest was the most populated, productive and with the highest economic expectations.<sup id="cite_ref-mdc.ulpgc_1_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mdc.ulpgc_1-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> La Laguna would be considered the <i>de facto</i> capital of the archipelago<sup id="cite_ref-ref_duplicada_2_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ref_duplicada_2-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> until the official status of the capital of Canary Islands in the city of Santa Cruz de Tenerife was confirmed in the 19th century, due in part to the constant controversies and rivalries between the bourgeoisies of San Crist\xc3\xb3bal de La Laguna and Las Palmas de Gran Canaria for the economic, political and institutional hegemony of the archipelago.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Already in 1723, the Captain General of the Canary Islands <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lorenzo_Fernandez_de_Villavicencio&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lorenzo Fernandez de Villavicencio (page does not exist)">Lorenzo Fernandez de Villavicencio</a> had moved the headquarters of the General Captaincy of the Canary Islands from San Crist\xc3\xb3bal de La Laguna to Santa Cruz de Tenerife. This decision continued without pleasing the society of the island of Gran Canaria.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> It would be after the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Canary_Islands" title="Province of Canary Islands">Province of Canary Islands</a> in November 1833 in which Santa Cruz would become the first fully official capital of the Canary Islands (<i><a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">De jure</a></i> and not of <i>de facto</i> as happened previously).<sup id="cite_ref-Real_Decreto_wikisource_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Real_Decreto_wikisource-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Real_Decreto_Canarias_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Real_Decreto_Canarias-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Santa Cruz de Tenerife would be the capital of the Canary archipelago until during the Government of General <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Primo_de_Rivera" title="Miguel Primo de Rivera">Primo de Rivera</a> in 1927 the Province of Canary Islands was split in two provinces: <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Las_Palmas" title="Province of Las Palmas">Las Palmas</a> with capital in Las Palmas de Gran Canaria, and <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Province of Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a> with capital in the homonymous city.\n</p><p>Finally, with the Statute of Autonomy of the Canary Islands in 1982 and the creation of the Autonomous Community of the Canary Islands, the capital of the archipelago between Las Palmas de Gran Canaria and Santa Cruz de Tenerife is fixed, which is how it remains today.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="Demographics of the Canary Islands">Demographics of the Canary Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islanders" title="Canary Islanders">Canary Islanders</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_immigration_to_Cuba" title="Spanish immigration to Cuba">Spanish immigration to Cuba</a></div>\n<table class="toccolours" style="text-align:center;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb"> 2011<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup></th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">2,082,655</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">\xe2\x88\x921.69%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px"> 2014<sup id="cite_ref-Desciende_la_poblaci\xc3\xb3n_en_Canarias_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Desciende_la_poblaci\xc3\xb3n_en_Canarias-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">2,104,815</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+0.35%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px"> 2015<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup></th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">2,128,647</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+1.13%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px"> 2017 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">2,154,905</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+0.61%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px"> 2018<sup id="cite_ref-BOE_pop_2018_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOE_pop_2018-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">2,127,685</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">\xe2\x88\x921.26%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px"> 2019 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">2,153,389</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+1.21%</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The Canary Islands have a population of 2,153,389 inhabitants (2019), making it the eighth most populous of Spain\'s <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous communities">autonomous communities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BOE_pop_2019_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOE_pop_2019-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The total area of the archipelago is 7,493&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (2,893&#160;sq&#160;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-extension_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-extension-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> resulting in a population density of 287.4 inhabitants per square kilometre.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" Kingdom</a></td>\n<td>25,339</td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2"><b><a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a></b></td>\n<td>38,768</td>\n<td>1.8\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2"><a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a></td>\n<td>24,268</td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2"><b><a href="/wiki/Asia" colspan="2"><b><a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a></b></td>\n<td>314</td>\n<td>0.0\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="2">Total</th>\n<th align="center">2,153,389</th>\n<th align="center">100.0\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="4" style="text-align:left;"><small>Source</small><sup id="cite_ref-ine_pop_19_birthplace_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ine_pop_19_birthplace-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ine_pop_cn_19_birthplace_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ine_pop_cn_19_birthplace-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The Canarian population includes long-tenured residents and new waves of mainland Spanish immigrants, as well as foreign-born populations.<sup id="cite_ref-canarias7.es_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-canarias7.es-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> In 2019 the total population was 2,153,389, of which 72.1% were native Canary Islanders.<sup id="cite_ref-ine_pop_cn_19_birthplace_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ine_pop_cn_19_birthplace-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> A total of 80.6%, or 1,735,457, were born in Spain and 19.4%, or 417,932, were born outside the country. Of these, the majority are from the Americas, mainly from <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> (66,593), <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> (41,807) and <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> (31,368). There are also almost 40,000 people from Africa, the majority from <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> (24,281).<sup id="cite_ref-canarias7.es_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-canarias7.es-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ine_pop_19_birthplace_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ine_pop_19_birthplace-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population_of_the_individual_islands">Population of the individual islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Population of the individual islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The population of the islands according to the 2019 data are:<sup id="cite_ref-BOE_pop_2019_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOE_pop_2019-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a> \xe2\x80\x93 917,841</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a> \xe2\x80\x93 851,231</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lanzarote" title="Lanzarote">Lanzarote</a> \xe2\x80\x93 152,289 (including the population of <a href="/wiki/La_Graciosa" class="mw-redirect" title="La Graciosa">La Graciosa</a>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura" title="Fuerteventura">Fuerteventura</a> \xe2\x80\x93 116,886</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/La_Palma" title="La Palma">La Palma</a> \xe2\x80\x93 82,671</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/La_Gomera" title="La Gomera">La Gomera</a> \xe2\x80\x93 21,503</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/El_Hierro" title="El Hierro">El Hierro</a> \xe2\x80\x93 10,968</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Canary_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Religion in Canary Islands">Religion in Canary Islands</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Candelaria_Basilica.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Candelaria_Basilica.jpg/220px-Candelaria_Basilica.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Candelaria_Basilica.jpg/330px-Candelaria_Basilica.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Candelaria_Basilica.jpg/440px-Candelaria_Basilica.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2307" data-file-height="1689" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Candelaria_Basilica.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_Candelaria" title="Basilica of Candelaria">Basilica of the Virgin of Candelaria</a> (Patroness of the Canary Islands) in <a href="/wiki/Candelaria,_Tenerife" title="Candelaria, Tenerife">Candelaria</a>, Tenerife</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a> branch of <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> has been the majority religion in the archipelago for more than five centuries, ever since the <a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="Conquest of the Canary Islands">Conquest of the Canary Islands</a>. There are also several other religious communities.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_Catholic_Church">Roman Catholic Church</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Roman Catholic Church">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The overwhelming majority of native Canarians are <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> (76.7%)<sup id="cite_ref-CIS2019Canarias_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIS2019Canarias-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> with various smaller foreign-born populations of other Christian beliefs such as <a href="/wiki/Protestants" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestants">Protestants</a>.\n</p><p>The appearance of the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_of_Candelaria" title="Virgin of Candelaria">Virgin of Candelaria</a> (Patron of Canary Islands) was credited with moving the Canary Islands toward Christianity. Two Catholic saints were born in the Canary Islands: <a href="/wiki/Peter_of_Saint_Joseph_de_Betancur" title="Peter of Saint Joseph de Betancur">Peter of Saint Joseph de Betancur</a><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_Anchieta" class="mw-redirect" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 de Anchieta">Jos\xc3\xa9 de Anchieta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Both born on the island of Tenerife, they were respectively missionaries in <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">Guatemala</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>.\n</p><p>The Canary Islands are divided into two Catholic dioceses, each governed by a bishop:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Canarias" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Canarias">Di\xc3\xb3cesis Canariense</a>: Includes the islands of the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Las_Palmas" title="Province of Las Palmas">Eastern Province</a>: Gran Canaria, Fuerteventura and Lanzarote. Its capital was San Marcial El Rubic\xc3\xb3n (1404) and <a href="/wiki/Las_Palmas" title="Las Palmas">Las Palmas de Gran Canaria</a> (1483\xe2\x80\x93present). There was a previous bishopric which was based in <a href="/wiki/Telde" title="Telde">Telde</a>, but it was later abolished.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_San_Crist%C3%B3bal_de_La_Laguna" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of San Crist\xc3\xb3bal de La Laguna">Di\xc3\xb3cesis Nivariense</a>: Includes the islands of the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Santa Cruz de Tenerife (province)">western province</a>: Tenerife, La Palma, La Gomera and El Hierro. Its capital is <a href="/wiki/San_Crist%C3%B3bal_de_La_Laguna" title="San Crist\xc3\xb3bal de La Laguna">San Crist\xc3\xb3bal de La Laguna</a> (1819\xe2\x80\x93present).</li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_religions">Other religions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Other religions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Separate from the overwhelming Christian majority are a minority of <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-laopinion.es_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-laopinion.es-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Among the followers of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Federation_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="Islamic Federation of the Canary Islands">Islamic Federation of the Canary Islands</a> exists to represent the Islamic community in the Canary Islands as well as to provide practical support to members of the Islamic community.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other religious faiths represented include <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Jehovah\'s Witnesses</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-laopinion.es_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-laopinion.es-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Minority religions are also present such as the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Guanche_People" title="Church of the Guanche People">Church of the Guanche People</a> which is classified as a <a href="/wiki/Modern_Paganism" title="Modern Paganism">neo-pagan</a> native religion.<sup id="cite_ref-laopinion.es_97-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-laopinion.es-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Also present are <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-laopinion.es_97-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-laopinion.es-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-laopinion.es_97-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-laopinion.es-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bah\xc3\xa1\xca\xbc\xc3\xad Faith">Bah\xc3\xa1\xca\xbc\xc3\xad</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-laopinion.es_97-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-laopinion.es-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/African_religion" class="mw-redirect" title="African religion">African religion</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-laopinion.es_97-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-laopinion.es-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_religions" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese religions">Chinese religions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-laopinion.es_97-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-laopinion.es-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics">Statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The distribution of beliefs in 2012 according to the CIS Barometer Autonomy was as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Catholic 84.9%</li>\n<li>Atheist/Agnostic/Unbeliever 12.3%</li>\n<li>Other religions 1.7%</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population_genetics">Population genetics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Population genetics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Canarian_people#Population_genetics" class="mw-redirect" title="Canarian people">Canarian people \xc2\xa7&#160;Population genetics</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Islands">Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Ordered from west to east, the Canary Islands are <a href="/wiki/El_Hierro" title="El Hierro">El Hierro</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Palma" title="La Palma">La Palma</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Gomera" title="La Gomera">La Gomera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura" title="Fuerteventura">Fuerteventura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lanzarote" title="Lanzarote">Lanzarote</a> and <a href="/wiki/La_Graciosa" class="mw-redirect" title="La Graciosa">La Graciosa</a>. In addition, north of Lanzarote are the islets of <a href="/wiki/Monta%C3%B1a_Clara" title="Monta\xc3\xb1a Clara">Monta\xc3\xb1a Clara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alegranza" title="Alegranza">Alegranza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roque_del_Este" title="Roque del Este">Roque del Este</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roque_del_Oeste" title="Roque del Oeste">Roque del Oeste</a>, belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Chinijo_Archipelago" title="Chinijo Archipelago">Chinijo Archipelago</a>, and northeast of Fuerteventura is the islet of <a href="/wiki/Lobos_Island" title="Lobos Island">Lobos</a>. There are also a series of small adjacent rocks in the Canary Islands: the <a href="/wiki/Roques_de_Anaga" title="Roques de Anaga">Roques de Anaga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roque_de_Garachico" title="Roque de Garachico">Garachico</a> and Fasnia in Tenerife, and those of Salmor and <a href="/wiki/Bonanza" title="Bonanza">Bonanza</a> in El Hierro.\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed center">\n\t<li class="gallerycaption">The Canary Islands</li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 125.33333333333px"><div style="width: 125.33333333333px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 125.33333333333px"><div style="width: 125.33333333333px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 123.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:-0.16666666666667px auto;"><a class="gallerybox" style="width: 125.33333333333px"><div style="width: 125.33333333333px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 123.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:-0.16666666666667px auto;"><a
