Graciosa</a>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="El_Hierro">El Hierro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: El Hierro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/El_Hierro" title="El Hierro">El Hierro</a></div>\n<p>El Hierro, the westernmost island, covers 268.71&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (103.75&#160;sq&#160;mi), making it the second smallest of the major islands, and the least populous with 10,798 inhabitants. The whole island was declared Reserve of the Biosphere in 2000. Its capital is <a href="/wiki/Valverde,_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Valverde, Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Valverde</a>. Also known as Ferro, it was once believed to be the westernmost land in the world.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fuerteventura">Fuerteventura</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Fuerteventura">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura" title="Fuerteventura">Fuerteventura</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:808px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:Barranco_de_Pecenescal_-_Fuerteventura.jpg" class="image" title="Barranco de Pecenescal \xe2\x80\x93 Fuerteventura"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Barranco_de_Pecenescal_-_Fuerteventura.jpg/800px-Barranco_de_Pecenescal_-_Fuerteventura.jpg" decoding="async" width="800" height="170" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Barranco_de_Pecenescal_-_Fuerteventura.jpg/1200px-Barranco_de_Pecenescal_-_Fuerteventura.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Barranco_de_Pecenescal_-_Fuerteventura.jpg/1600px-Barranco_de_Pecenescal_-_Fuerteventura.jpg 2x" data-file-width="11163" data-file-height="2373" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barranco_de_Pecenescal_-_Fuerteventura.jpg" title="File:Barranco de Pecenescal - Fuerteventura.jpg"> </a></div>Barranco de Pecenescal \xe2\x80\x93 Fuerteventura</div></div></div>\n<p>Fuerteventura, with a surface of 1,660&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (640&#160;sq&#160;mi), is the second-most extensive island of the archipelago. It has been declared a <a href="/wiki/Biosphere_reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="Biosphere reserve">Biosphere reserve</a> by <a href="/wiki/Unesco" class="mw-redirect" title="Unesco">Unesco</a>. It has a population of 113,275. Being also the most ancient of the islands, it is the one that is more eroded: its highest point is the Peak of the Bramble, at a height of 807 metres (2,648 feet). Its capital is <a href="/wiki/Puerto_del_Rosario" title="Puerto del Rosario">Puerto del Rosario</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gran_Canaria">Gran Canaria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Gran Canaria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pueblo_de_Fataga.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Pueblo_de_Fataga.jpg/220px-Pueblo_de_Fataga.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Pueblo_de_Fataga.jpg/330px-Pueblo_de_Fataga.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Pueblo_de_Fataga.jpg/440px-Pueblo_de_Fataga.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2967" data-file-height="1650" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pueblo_de_Fataga.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of <a href="/wiki/Fataga" title="Fataga">Fataga</a>, Gran Canaria</div></div></div>\n<p>Gran Canaria has 846,717 inhabitants. The capital, <a href="/wiki/Las_Palmas" title="Las Palmas">Las Palmas de Gran Canaria</a> (377,203 inhabitants), is the most populous city and shares the status of capital of the Canaries with Santa Cruz de Tenerife. Gran Canaria\'s surface area is 1,560&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (600&#160;sq&#160;mi). In center of the island lie the Roque Nublo 1,813 metres (5,948 feet) and Pico de las Nieves ("Peak of Snow") 1,949 metres (6,394 feet). In the south of island are the Maspalomas Dunes (Gran Canaria), these are the biggest tourist attractions.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="La_Gomera">La Gomera</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: La Gomera">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/La_Gomera" title="La Gomera">La Gomera</a></div>\n<p>La Gomera has an area of 369.76&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (142.77&#160;sq&#160;mi) and is the second least populous island with 21,136 inhabitants. Geologically it is one of the oldest of the archipelago. The insular capital is <a href="/wiki/San_Sebastian_de_La_Gomera" class="mw-redirect" title="San Sebastian de La Gomera">San Sebastian de La Gomera</a>. Garajonay\'s National Park is located on the island.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lanzarote">Lanzarote</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Lanzarote">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lanzarote" title="Lanzarote">Lanzarote</a></div>\n<p>Lanzarote is the easternmost island and one of the most ancient of the archipelago, and it has shown evidence of recent volcanic activity. It has a surface of 845.94&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (326.62&#160;sq&#160;mi), and a population of 149,183 inhabitants, including the adjacent islets of the Chinijo Archipelago. The capital is <a href="/wiki/Arrecife" title="Arrecife">Arrecife</a>, with 56,834 inhabitants.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Chinijo_Archipelago">Chinijo Archipelago</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Chinijo Archipelago">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Chinijo_Archipelago" title="Chinijo Archipelago">Chinijo Archipelago</a></div>\n<p>The Chinijo Archipelago includes the islands <a href="/wiki/La_Graciosa" class="mw-redirect" title="La Graciosa">La Graciosa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alegranza" title="Alegranza">Alegranza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monta%C3%B1a_Clara" title="Monta\xc3\xb1a Clara">Monta\xc3\xb1a Clara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roque_del_Este" title="Roque del Este">Roque del Este</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roque_del_Oeste" title="Roque del Oeste">Roque del Oeste</a>. It has a surface of 40.8&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (15.8&#160;sq&#160;mi), and a population of 658 inhabitants all of them on La Graciosa. With 29&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (11&#160;sq&#160;mi), La Graciosa, is the smallest inhabited island of the Canaries, and the major island of the Chinijo Archipelago.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="La_Palma">La Palma</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: La Palma">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/La_Palma" title="La Palma">La Palma</a></div>\n<p>La Palma, with 81,863 inhabitants covering an area of 708.32&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (273.48&#160;sq&#160;mi), is in its entirety a biosphere reserve. It shows no recent signs of volcanic activity, even though the volcano <a href="/wiki/Tenegu%C3%ADa" title="Tenegu\xc3\xada">Tenegu\xc3\xada</a> entered into eruption last in 1971. In addition, it is the second-highest island of the Canaries, with the Roque de los Muchachos 2,423 metres (7,949 feet) as highest point. <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_La_Palma" title="Santa Cruz de La Palma">Santa Cruz de La Palma</a> (known to those on the island as simply "Santa Cruz") is its capital.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tenerife">Tenerife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Tenerife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Urville-Laguna.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Urville-Laguna.jpg/220px-Urville-Laguna.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Urville-Laguna.jpg/330px-Urville-Laguna.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Urville-Laguna.jpg/440px-Urville-Laguna.jpg 2x" data-file-width="672" data-file-height="504" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Urville-Laguna.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/San_Crist%C3%B3bal_de_La_Laguna" title="San Crist\xc3\xb3bal de La Laguna">San Crist\xc3\xb3bal de La Laguna</a> in 1880 (Tenerife)</div></div></div>\n<p>Tenerife is, with its area of 2,034&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (785&#160;sq&#160;mi), the most extensive island of the Canary Islands. In addition, with 904,713 inhabitants it is the most populated island of the archipelago and Spain. Two of the islands\' principal cities are located on it: The capital, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Crist%C3%B3bal_de_La_Laguna" title="San Crist\xc3\xb3bal de La Laguna">San Crist\xc3\xb3bal de La Laguna</a> (a World Heritage Site). San Crist\xc3\xb3bal de La Laguna, the second city of the island is home to the oldest university in the Canary Islands, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_La_Laguna" title="University of La Laguna">University of La Laguna</a>. <a href="/wiki/Teide" title="Teide">Teide</a>, with its 3,715 metres (12,188 feet) is the highest peak of Spain and also a World Heritage Site. Tenerife is the site of the <a href="/wiki/Tenerife_airport_disaster" title="Tenerife airport disaster">worst air disaster</a> in the history of aviation, in which 583 people were killed in the collision of two Boeing 747s on 27 March 1977.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="La_Graciosa">La Graciosa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: La Graciosa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/La_Graciosa" class="mw-redirect" title="La Graciosa">La Graciosa</a></div>\n<p>Graciosa Island or commonly La Graciosa is a volcanic island in the Canary Islands of Spain, located 2&#160;km (1.2&#160;mi) north of the island of Lanzarote across the Strait of El R\xc3\xado. It was formed by the Canary hotspot. The island is part of the Chinijo Archipelago and the Chinijo Archipelago Natural Park (Parque Natural del Archipi\xc3\xa9lago Chinijo). It is administrated by the municipality of Teguise. In 2018 La Graciosa officially became the eighth Canary Island.<sup id="cite_ref-Monz\xc3\xb3n2019_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Monz\xc3\xb3n2019-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Before then, La Graciosa had the status of an islet, administratively dependent on the island of Lanzarote. It is the smallest and least populated of the main islands, with a population of about 700 people.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Data">Data</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Data">edit</a><span align="center">\xe2\x80\x93\n</td>\n<td align="center">0.015\n</td>\n<td align="center">\xe2\x80\x93\n</td>\n<td align="center">\xe2\x80\x93\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy_and_environment">Economy and environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Economy and environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_the_Canary_Islands" title="Tourism in the Canary Islands">Tourism in the Canary Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_based_in_the_Canary_Islands" title="List of companies based in the Canary Islands">List of companies based in the Canary Islands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Island_country#Natural_resources" title="Island country">Island country \xc2\xa7&#160;Natural resources</a></div>\n<table class="toccolours" cellpadding="2" cellspacing="0" style="float:right; margin:0 0 1em 1em; font-size:95%;">\n<caption><b><a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_the_Canary_Islands" title="Tourism in the Canary Islands">Tourism in the Canary Islands</a></b><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">Year\n</th>\n<th style="text-align:center;border-bottom:1px #aaa solid;">Visitors\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2009<br /><span style="font-size:85%;">(Jan\xe2\x80\x93Jun)</span></td>\n<td>4,002,013\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2008</td>\n<td>9,210,509\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2007</td>\n<td>9,326,116\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2006</td>\n<td>9,530,039\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2005</td>\n<td>9,276,963\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2004</td>\n<td>9,427,265\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2003</td>\n<td>9,836,785\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2002</td>\n<td>9,778,512\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2001</td>\n<td>10,137,205\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">2000</td>\n<td>9,975,977\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">1993</td>\n<td>6,545,396\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="text-align:center;border-top:1px #aaa solid;">Largest by<br />Country <span style="font-size:85%;">(2008)</span>\n</th>\n<th style="text-align:center;border-top:1px #aaa solid;">Population\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">Germany</td>\n<td>2,498,847\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;">United Kingdom</td>\n<td>3,355,942\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dunas_de_Maspalomas.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Dunas_de_Maspalomas.jpg/220px-Dunas_de_Maspalomas.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="121" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Dunas_de_Maspalomas.jpg/330px-Dunas_de_Maspalomas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Dunas_de_Maspalomas.jpg/440px-Dunas_de_Maspalomas.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1268" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dunas_de_Maspalomas.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The dunes of <a href="/wiki/Maspalomas" title="Maspalomas">Maspalomas</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a> is one of the tourist attractions</div></div></div>\n<p>The economy is based primarily on <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Spain" title="Tourism in Spain">tourism</a>, which makes up 32% of the GDP. The Canaries receive about 12&#160;million tourists per year. Construction makes up nearly 20% of the GDP and tropical agriculture, primarily bananas and tobacco, are grown for export to Europe and the Americas. Ecologists are concerned that the resources, especially in the more <a href="/wiki/Arid" title="Arid">arid</a> islands, are being <a href="/wiki/Overexploited" class="mw-redirect" title="Overexploited">overexploited</a> but there are still many agricultural resources like <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">tomatoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">potatoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Onion" title="Onion">onions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cochineal" title="Cochineal">cochineal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grape" title="Grape">grapes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vine" title="Vine">vines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_dactylifera" class="mw-redirect" title="Phoenix dactylifera">dates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange_(fruit)" title="Orange (fruit)">oranges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lemon" title="Lemon">lemons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ficus" title="Ficus">figs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barley" title="Barley">barley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apricot" title="Apricot">apricots</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peach" title="Peach">peaches</a> and <a href="/wiki/Almond" title="Almond">almonds</a>.\n</p><p>Water resources are also being overexploited, due to the high water usage by tourists.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Also, some islands (such as Gran Canaria and Tenerife) <a href="/wiki/Groundwater_extraction" class="mw-redirect" title="Groundwater extraction">overexploit the ground water</a>. This is done in such degree that, according to European and Spanish legal regulations, the current situation is not acceptable. To address the problems, good governance and a change in the water use paradigm have been proposed. These solutions depend largely on <a href="/wiki/Water_conservation" title="Water conservation">controlling water use</a> and on demand management. As this is administratively difficult and politically unpalatable, most action is currently directed at increasing the public offer of water through import from outside; a decision which is economically, politically and environmentally questionable.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>To bring in revenue for environmental protection, innovation, training and water sanitation a <a href="/wiki/Tourist_tax" title="Tourist tax">tourist tax</a> was considered in 2018, along with a doubling of the <a href="/wiki/Ecotax" title="Ecotax">ecotax</a> and restrictions on holiday rents in the zones with the greatest pressure of demand.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The economy is <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">\xe2\x82\xac</a> 25&#160;billion (2001 GDP figures). The islands experienced continuous growth during a 20-year period, up until 2001, at a rate of approximately 5% annually. This growth was fueled mainly by huge amounts of <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a>, mostly to develop tourism real estate (hotels and apartments), and European Funds (near \xe2\x82\xac11&#160;billion in the period from 2000 to 2007), since the Canary Islands are labelled Region Objective 1 (eligible for euro structural funds).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Additionally, the EU allows the Canary Islands Government to offer special tax concessions for investors who incorporate under the Zona Especial Canaria (ZEC) regime and create more than five jobs.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Spain gave permission in August 2014 for <a href="/wiki/Repsol" title="Repsol">Repsol</a> and its partners to explore <a href="/wiki/Oil" title="Oil">oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> prospects off the Canary Islands, involving an investment of \xe2\x82\xac7.5&#160;billion over four years, to commence at the end of 2016. Repsol at the time said the area could ultimately produce 100,000 barrels of oil a day, which would meet 10 percent of Spain\'s energy needs.<sup id="cite_ref-RepsolCanary_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RepsolCanary-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> However, the analysis of samples obtained did not show the necessary volume nor quality to consider future extraction, and the project was scrapped.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Despite currently having very high dependence on fossil fuels, research on the renewable energy potential concluded that a high potential for renewable energy technologies exists on the archipelago. This, in such extent even that a scenario pathway to 100% renewable energy supply by 2050 has been put forward.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Canary Islands have great natural attractions, climate and <a href="/wiki/Beach" title="Beach">beaches</a> make the islands a major tourist destination, being visited each year by about 12&#160;million people (11,986,059 in 2007, noting 29% of <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Britons</a>, 22% of Spanish, not residents of the Canaries, and 21% of <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germans</a>). Among the islands, Tenerife has the largest number of tourists received annually, followed by Gran Canaria and Lanzarote.<sup id="cite_ref-gobiernodecanarias1_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gobiernodecanarias1-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-webtenerife1_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-webtenerife1-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The archipelago\'s principal tourist attraction is the <a href="/wiki/Teide_National_Park" title="Teide National Park">Teide National Park</a> (in Tenerife) where the highest mountain in Spain and third largest <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcano</a> in the world (Mount <a href="/wiki/Teide" title="Teide">Teide</a>), receives over 2.8&#160;million visitors annually.<sup id="cite_ref-webtenerife2_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-webtenerife2-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The combination of high mountains, proximity to Europe, and clean air has made the <a href="/wiki/Roque_de_los_Muchachos" title="Roque de los Muchachos">Roque de los Muchachos</a> peak (on La Palma island) a leading location for <a href="/wiki/Telescope" title="Telescope">telescopes</a> like the <a href="/wiki/Grantecan" class="mw-redirect" title="Grantecan">Grantecan</a>.\n</p><p>The islands, as an autonomous region of Spain, are in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>. They are in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Customs_Union" title="European Union Customs Union">European Union Customs Union</a> but outside the <a href="/wiki/VAT" class="mw-redirect" title="VAT">VAT</a> area,<sup id="cite_ref-territories_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-territories-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Instead of VAT there is a local Sales Tax (IGIC) which has a general rate of 7%, an increased tax rate of 13.5%, a reduced tax rate of 3% and a zero tax rate for certain basic need products and services. Consequently, some products are subject to additional VAT if being exported from the islands into mainland Spain or the rest of the EU.\n</p><p>Canarian time is <a href="/wiki/Western_European_Time" title="Western European Time">Western European Time</a> (WET) (or <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Mean_Time" title="Greenwich Mean Time">GMT</a>; in summer one hour ahead of GMT). So Canarian time is one hour behind that of mainland Spain and the same as that of the UK, Ireland and mainland Portugal all year round.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism_statistics">Tourism statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Tourism statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The number of tourists who visited the Canary Islands had been in 2018 16,150,054 and in the year 2019 15,589,290.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption><b>Number of tourists who visited statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: GDP statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Gross Domestic Product (GDP) in the Canary Islands in 2015 was 40,922,914. The figure by islands is as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Tenerife - 17 614 585</li>\n<li>Gran Canaria - 15 812 222</li>\n<li>Lanzarote - 3 203 394</li>\n<li>Fuerteventura - 2 298 120</li>\n<li>La Palma - 1 422 949</li>\n<li>La Gomera - 393 845</li>\n<li>El Hierro - 177 799</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Las_palmas_gran_canaria_parque_san_telmo_2005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Las_palmas_gran_canaria_parque_san_telmo_2005.jpg/220px-Las_palmas_gran_canaria_parque_san_telmo_2005.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Las_palmas_gran_canaria_parque_san_telmo_2005.jpg/330px-Las_palmas_gran_canaria_parque_san_telmo_2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Las_palmas_gran_canaria_parque_san_telmo_2005.jpg/440px-Las_palmas_gran_canaria_parque_san_telmo_2005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Las_palmas_gran_canaria_parque_san_telmo_2005.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bus Station\xe2\x80\x94<i>Estaci\xc3\xb3n de Guaguas</i> also known as <i>El Hoyo</i> (The hole), on the left, out of the image\xe2\x80\x94at San Telmo Park, <a href="/wiki/Las_Palmas_de_Gran_Canaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Palmas de Gran Canaria">Las Palmas de Gran Canaria</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tranviadetenerife.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Tranviadetenerife.JPG/220px-Tranviadetenerife.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Tranviadetenerife.JPG/330px-Tranviadetenerife.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Tranviadetenerife.JPG/440px-Tranviadetenerife.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tranviadetenerife.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tenerife_Tram" title="Tenerife Tram">Tenerife Tram</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The Canary Islands have eight airports altogether, two of the main ports of Spain, and an extensive network of <a href="/wiki/Highways_in_Spain" title="Highways in Spain">autopistas</a> (highways) and other roads. For a road map see multimap.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Traffic_congestion" title="Traffic congestion">Traffic congestion</a> is sometimes a problem in Tenerife and on Grand Canaria.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are large ferry boats that link islands as well as fast ferries linking most of the islands. Both types can transport large numbers of passengers and cargo (including vehicles). Fast ferries are made of aluminium and powered by modern and efficient diesel engines, while conventional ferries have a steel hull and are powered by heavy oil. Fast ferries travel relatively quickly (in excess of 30&#160;kn (56&#160;km/h; 35&#160;mph)) and are a faster method of transportation than the conventional ferry (some<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="does &quot;some&quot; mean &quot;approximately&quot;? Or does it mean &quot;some of the ferries&quot;? (December 2018)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> 20&#160;kn (37&#160;km/h; 23&#160;mph)). A typical ferry ride between La Palma and Tenerife may take up to eight hours or more while a fast ferry takes about two and a half hours and between Tenerife and Gran Canaria can be about one hour.\n</p><p>The largest airport is the <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria_Airport" title="Gran Canaria Airport">Gran Canaria Airport</a>. Tenerife has two airports, <a href="/wiki/Tenerife_North_Airport" title="Tenerife North Airport">Tenerife North Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tenerife_South_Airport" title="Tenerife South Airport">Tenerife South Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The island of Tenerife gathers the highest passenger movement of all the Canary Islands through its two airports.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> The two main islands (Tenerife and Gran Canaria) receive the greatest number of passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Tenerife 6,204,499 passengers and Gran Canaria 5,011,176 passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Las_Palmas" title="Port of Las Palmas">port of Las Palmas</a> is first in freight traffic in the islands,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> while the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Port of Santa Cruz de Tenerife">port of Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a> is the first fishing port with approximately 7,500 tons of fish caught, according to the Spanish government publication Statistical Yearbook of State Ports. Similarly, it is the second port in Spain as regards ship traffic, only surpassed by the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Algeciras" title="Port of Algeciras">Port of Algeciras</a> Bay.<sup id="cite_ref-puertos.es_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-puertos.es-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> The port\'s facilities include a border inspection post (BIP) approved by the European Union, which is responsible for inspecting all types of imports from third countries or exports to countries outside the European Economic Area. The port of <a href="/wiki/Los_Cristianos" title="Los Cristianos">Los Cristianos</a> (Tenerife) has the greatest number of passengers recorded in the Canary Islands, followed by the port of Santa Cruz de Tenerife.<sup id="cite_ref-www2.gobiernodecanarias.org_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www2.gobiernodecanarias.org-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> The Port of Las Palmas is the third port in the islands in passengers and first in number of vehicles transported.<sup id="cite_ref-www2.gobiernodecanarias.org_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www2.gobiernodecanarias.org-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/SS_America_(1939)" title="SS America (1939)">SS America</a> was beached at the Canary islands on 18 January 1994. However, the ocean liner broke apart after the course of several years and eventually sank beneath the surface.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail_transport">Rail transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Rail transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Tenerife_Tram" title="Tenerife Tram">Tenerife Tram</a> opened in 2007 and is currently the only one in the Canary Islands, travelling between the cities of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Crist%C3%B3bal_de_La_Laguna" title="San Crist\xc3\xb3bal de La Laguna">San Crist\xc3\xb3bal de La Laguna</a>.\n</p><p>Three more railway lines are being planned for the Canary Islands:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Line\n</th>\n<th>Island\n</th>\n<th>Terminus A\n</th>\n<th>Terminus B\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Tren_de_Gran_Canaria" title="Tren de Gran Canaria">Tren de Gran Canaria</a><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran title="Maspalomas">Maspalomas</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Tren_del_Sur" title="Tren del Sur">Tren del Sur</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Tenerife" Cruz de Tenerife</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Los_Realejos" title="Los Realejos">Los Realejos</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Tenerife_South_Airport" title="Tenerife South Airport">Tenerife South Airport</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Tenerife</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tenerife_North_Airport" title="Tenerife North Airport">Tenerife North Airport</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Tenerife</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lanzarote_Airport" title="Lanzarote Airport">C\xc3\xa9sar Manrique-Lanzarote Airport</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Lanzarote</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura_Airport" title="Fuerteventura Airport">Fuerteventura Airport</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Fuerteventura</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria_Airport" title="Gran Canaria Airport">Gran Canaria Airport</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Gran Canaria</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/La_Palma_Airport" title="La Palma Airport">La Palma Airport</a> \xe2\x80\x93 La Palma</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/La_Gomera_Airport" title="La Gomera Airport">La Gomera Airport</a> \xe2\x80\x93 La Gomera</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/El_Hierro_Airport" title="El Hierro Airport">El Hierro Airport</a> \xe2\x80\x93 El Hierro<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ports">Ports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Gomera</li>\n<li>Port of La Estaca \xe2\x80\x93 El Hierro</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Port_of_Las_Palmas" title="Port of Las Palmas">Port of Las Palmas</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Gran Canaria</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Port_of_Arinaga" title="Port of Arinaga">Port of Arinaga</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Gran Canaria</li>\n<li>Port of Agaete \xe2\x80\x93 Gran Canaria</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Port_of_Los_Cristianos" Tenerife</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Tenerife</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Port_of_Garachico" title="Port of Garachico">Port of Garachico</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Tenerife</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Port_of_Granadilla" title="Port of Granadilla">Port of Granadilla</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Tenerife</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Spain#Canary_Islands" title="List of hospitals in Spain">List of hospitals in Spain \xc2\xa7&#160;Canary Islands</a></div>\n<p>The <i>Servicio Canario de Salud</i> is an autonomous body of administrative nature attached to the Ministry responsible for Health of the Government of the Canary Islands. The majority of the archipelago\'s hospitals belong to this organization:<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Hospital Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora de los Reyes \xe2\x80\x93 El Hierro</li>\n<li>Hospital General de La Palma \xe2\x80\x93 La Palma</li>\n<li>Hospital Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora de Guadalupe \xe2\x80\x93 La Gomera</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hospital_Universitario_Nuestra_Se%C3%B1ora_de_Candelaria" title="Hospital Universitario Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora de Candelaria">Hospital Universitario Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora de Candelaria</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Tenerife</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hospital_Universitario_de_Canarias" title="Hospital Universitario de Canarias">Hospital Universitario de Canarias</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Tenerife</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hospital_del_Sur_de_Tenerife" title="Hospital del Sur de Tenerife">Hospital del Sur de Tenerife</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Tenerife</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hospital_del_Norte_de_Tenerife" title="Hospital del Norte de Tenerife">Hospital del Norte de Tenerife</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Tenerife</li>\n<li>Hospital Universitario de Gran Canaria Doctor Negr\xc3\xadn \xe2\x80\x93 Gran Canaria</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hospital_Universitario_Insular_de_Gran_Canaria" title="Hospital Universitario Insular de Gran Canaria">Hospital Universitario Insular de Gran Canaria</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Gran Canaria</li>\n<li>Hospital General de Lanzarote Doctor Jos\xc3\xa9 Molina Orosa \xe2\x80\x93 Lanzarote</li>\n<li>Hospital General de Fuerteventura \xe2\x80\x93 Fuerteventura</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2012-01-10_14-53-40_Spain_Canarias_Cofete.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/2012-01-10_14-53-40_Spain_Canarias_Cofete.jpg/220px-2012-01-10_14-53-40_Spain_Canarias_Cofete.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/2012-01-10_14-53-40_Spain_Canarias_Cofete.jpg/330px-2012-01-10_14-53-40_Spain_Canarias_Cofete.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/2012-01-10_14-53-40_Spain_Canarias_Cofete.jpg/440px-2012-01-10_14-53-40_Spain_Canarias_Cofete.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4112" data-file-height="2741" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2012-01-10_14-53-40_Spain_Canarias_Cofete.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Euphorbia_canariensis" title="Euphorbia canariensis">Canary Island spurge</a> in Fuerteventura</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistoric_fauna">Prehistoric fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Prehistoric fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Canariomys_bravoi_skull.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Canariomys_bravoi_skull.JPG/220px-Canariomys_bravoi_skull.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Canariomys_bravoi_skull.JPG/330px-Canariomys_bravoi_skull.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Canariomys_bravoi_skull.JPG/440px-Canariomys_bravoi_skull.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1250" data-file-height="817" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Canariomys_bravoi_skull.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Skull of <i><a href="/wiki/Canariomys_bravoi" class="mw-redirect" title="Canariomys bravoi">Canariomys bravoi</a></i> (<i>Tenerife giant rat</i>). It was an endemic species that is now extinct.</div></div></div>\n<p>Before the arrival of the Aborigines, the Canary Islands was inhabited by endemic animals, such as some extinct; giant lizards (<i><a href="/wiki/Gallotia_goliath" title="Gallotia goliath">Gallotia goliath</a></i>), giant rats (<i><a href="/wiki/Canariomys_bravoi" class="mw-redirect" title="Canariomys bravoi">Canariomys bravoi</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Canariomys_tamarani" class="mw-redirect" title="Canariomys tamarani">Canariomys tamarani</a></i>)<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> and giant tortoises (<i><a href="/wiki/Geochelone_burchardi" class="mw-redirect" title="Geochelone burchardi">Geochelone burchardi</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Geochelone_vulcanica" class="mw-redirect" title="Geochelone vulcanica">Geochelone vulcanica</a></i>),<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> among others.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terrestrial_wildlife">Terrestrial wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Terrestrial wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_non-marine_molluscs_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="List of non-marine molluscs of the Canary Islands">List of non-marine molluscs of the Canary Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_reptiles_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="List of reptiles of the Canary Islands">List of reptiles of the Canary Islands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Lepidoptera_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="List of Lepidoptera of the Canary Islands">List of Lepidoptera of the Canary Islands</a></div>\n<p>With a range of habitats, the Canary Islands exhibit diverse plant species. The bird life includes European and African species, such as the <a href="/wiki/Black-bellied_sandgrouse" title="Black-bellied sandgrouse">black-bellied sandgrouse</a>; and a rich variety of <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a> (local) taxa including the:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Atlantic_canary" title="Atlantic canary">Canary</a></li>\n<li>Graja, a subspecies of <a href="/wiki/Red-billed_chough" title="Red-billed chough">red-billed chough</a> endemic to La Palma</li>\n<li>Blue chaffinch:\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria_blue_chaffinch" title="Gran Canaria blue chaffinch">Gran Canaria blue chaffinch</a> endemic to Gran Canaria</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tenerife_blue_chaffinch" title="Tenerife blue chaffinch">Tenerife blue chaffinch</a> endemic to Tenerife</li></ul></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands_chiffchaff" title="Canary Islands chiffchaff">Canary Islands chiffchaff</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura_chat" class="mw-redirect" title="Fuerteventura chat">Fuerteventura chat</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tenerife_goldcrest" title="Tenerife goldcrest">Tenerife goldcrest</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/La_Palma_chaffinch" title="La Palma chaffinch">La Palma chaffinch</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Canarian_Egyptian_vulture" class="mw-redirect" title="Canarian Egyptian vulture">Canarian Egyptian vulture</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bolle%27s_pigeon" title="Bolle&#39;s pigeon">Bolle\'s pigeon</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Laurel_pigeon" title="Laurel pigeon">Laurel pigeon</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Plain_swift" title="Plain swift">Plain swift</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Houbara_bustard" title="Houbara bustard">Houbara bustard</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Spider" title="Spider">Spiders</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Snake" title="Snake">Snakes</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Scorpion" title="Scorpion">Scorpions</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands_oystercatcher" title="Canary Islands oystercatcher">Canary Islands oystercatcher</a> (extinct)</li></ul>\n<p>Terrestrial fauna includes <a href="/wiki/Gecko" title="Gecko">geckos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wall_lizards" class="mw-redirect" title="Wall lizards">wall lizards</a>, and three endemic species of recently rediscovered and <a href="/wiki/Critically_endangered" class="mw-redirect" title="Critically endangered">critically endangered</a> giant lizard: the <a href="/wiki/El_Hierro_giant_lizard" title="El Hierro giant lizard">El Hierro giant lizard</a> (or <a href="/wiki/Roque_Chico_de_Salmor_giant_lizard" title="Roque Chico de Salmor giant lizard">Roque Chico de Salmor giant lizard</a>), <a href="/wiki/La_Gomera_giant_lizard" title="La Gomera giant lizard">La Gomera giant lizard</a>, and <a href="/wiki/La_Palma_giant_lizard" title="La Palma giant lizard">La Palma giant lizard</a>. Mammals include the <a href="/wiki/Canarian_shrew" title="Canarian shrew">Canarian shrew</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canary_big-eared_bat" title="Canary big-eared bat">Canary big-eared bat</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Algerian_hedgehog" class="mw-redirect" title="Algerian hedgehog">Algerian hedgehog</a> (which may have been introduced) and the more recently introduced <a href="/wiki/Mouflon" title="Mouflon">mouflon</a>. Some endemic mammals, the <a href="/wiki/Lava_mouse" title="Lava mouse">lava mouse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tenerife_giant_rat" title="Tenerife giant rat">Tenerife giant rat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria_giant_rat" title="Gran Canaria giant rat">Gran Canaria giant rat</a>, are extinct, as are the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands_quail" title="Canary Islands quail">Canary Islands quail</a>, <a href="/wiki/Long-legged_bunting" title="Long-legged bunting">long-legged bunting</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Canary_Islands_chiffchaff" title="Eastern Canary Islands chiffchaff">eastern Canary Islands chiffchaff</a> and the giant prehistoric tortoises; <a href="/wiki/Geochelone_burchardi" class="mw-redirect" title="Geochelone burchardi">Geochelone burchardi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geochelone_vulcanica" class="mw-redirect" title="Geochelone vulcanica">Geochelone vulcanica</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marine_life">Marine life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Marine life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Marine_life_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="Marine life of the Canary Islands">Marine life of the Canary Islands</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Caretta_caretta_060417w2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Caretta_caretta_060417w2.jpg/220px-Caretta_caretta_060417w2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Caretta_caretta_060417w2.jpg/330px-Caretta_caretta_060417w2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Caretta_caretta_060417w2.jpg/440px-Caretta_caretta_060417w2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1296" data-file-height="864" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Caretta_caretta_060417w2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Loggerhead_sea_turtle" title="Loggerhead sea turtle">loggerhead sea turtle</a>, by far the most common species of marine turtle in the Canary Islands.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Marine_life" title="Marine life">marine life</a> found in the Canary Islands is also varied, being a combination of <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">North Atlantic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">endemic</a> species. In recent years, the increasing popularity of both <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving" title="Scuba diving">scuba diving</a> and <a href="/wiki/Underwater_photography" title="Underwater photography">underwater photography</a> have provided biologists with much new information on the marine life of the islands.\n</p><p>Fish species found in the islands include many species of <a href="/wiki/Shark" title="Shark">shark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Batoidea" title="Batoidea">ray</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moray_eel" title="Moray eel">moray eel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sparidae" title="Sparidae">bream</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carangidae" title="Carangidae">jack</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grunt-fish" class="mw-redirect" title="Grunt-fish">grunt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scorpionfish" class="mw-redirect" title="Scorpionfish">scorpionfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Triggerfish" title="Triggerfish">triggerfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grouper" title="Grouper">grouper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goby" title="Goby">goby</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Blenny" class="mw-redirect" title="Blenny">blenny</a>. In addition, there are many invertebrate species, including <a href="/wiki/Sponge" title="Sponge">sponge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jellyfish" title="Jellyfish">jellyfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anemone" title="Anemone">anemone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crab" title="Crab">crab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mollusc" class="mw-redirect" title="Mollusc">mollusc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sea_urchin" title="Sea urchin">sea urchin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Starfish" title="Starfish">starfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holothuroidea" class="mw-redirect" title="Holothuroidea">sea cucumber</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coral" title="Coral">coral</a>.\n</p><p>There are a total of five different species of <a href="/wiki/Marine_turtle" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine turtle">marine turtle</a> that are sighted periodically in the islands, the most common of these being the <a href="/wiki/Endangered" class="mw-redirect" title="Endangered">endangered</a> <a href="/wiki/Loggerhead_sea_turtle" title="Loggerhead sea turtle">loggerhead sea turtle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> The other four are the <a href="/wiki/Green_sea_turtle" title="Green sea turtle">green sea turtle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hawksbill_sea_turtle" title="Hawksbill sea turtle">hawksbill sea turtle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leatherback_sea_turtle" title="Leatherback sea turtle">leatherback sea turtle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kemp%27s_ridley_sea_turtle" title="Kemp&#39;s ridley sea turtle">Kemp\'s ridley sea turtle</a>. Currently, there are no signs that any of these species breed in the islands, and so those seen in the water are usually <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/migration" class="extiw" title="wikt:migration">migrating</a>. However, it is believed that some of these species may have bred in the islands in the past, and there are records of several sightings of leatherback sea turtle on beaches in Fuerteventura, adding credibility to the theory.\n</p><p>Marine mammals include the large varieties of <a href="/wiki/Cetacean" class="mw-redirect" title="Cetacean">cetaceans</a> including rare and not well-known species (see more details in the <i><a href="/wiki/Marine_life_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="Marine life of the Canary Islands">Marine life of the Canary Islands</a></i>). <a href="/wiki/Hooded_seals" class="mw-redirect" title="Hooded seals">Hooded seals</a><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> have also been known to be vagrant in the Canary Islands every now and then. The Canary Islands were also formerly home to a population of the rarest <a href="/wiki/Pinniped" title="Pinniped">pinniped</a> in the world, the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_monk_seal" title="Mediterranean monk seal">Mediterranean monk seal</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Native_flora_gallery">Native flora gallery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Native flora gallery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 188.66666666667px"><div style="width: class="mw-headline" id="Holidays">Holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Holidays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Danza_de_Enanos_2015_PMBV.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Danza_de_Enanos_2015_PMBV.jpg/170px-Danza_de_Enanos_2015_PMBV.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Danza_de_Enanos_2015_PMBV.jpg/255px-Danza_de_Enanos_2015_PMBV.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Danza_de_Enanos_2015_PMBV.jpg/340px-Danza_de_Enanos_2015_PMBV.jpg 2x" data-file-width="428" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Danza_de_Enanos_2015_PMBV.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Dance of the Dwarves is one of the most important acts of the Lustral Festivities of the <i>Bajada de la Virgen de las Nieves</i> in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_La_Palma" title="Santa Cruz de La Palma">Santa Cruz de La Palma</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bailarines.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Bailarines.jpg/170px-Bailarines.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="282" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Bailarines.jpg/255px-Bailarines.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Bailarines.jpg/340px-Bailarines.jpg 2x" data-file-width="449" data-file-height="745" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bailarines.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dancers with typical costume in El Tamaduste (<a href="/wiki/El_Hierro" title="El Hierro">El Hierro</a>).</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Banda_de_Agaete_en_la_Tra%C3%ADda_del_Agua.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Banda_de_Agaete_en_la_Tra%C3%ADda_del_Agua.jpg/170px-Banda_de_Agaete_en_la_Tra%C3%ADda_del_Agua.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Banda_de_Agaete_en_la_Tra%C3%ADda_del_Agua.jpg/255px-Banda_de_Agaete_en_la_Tra%C3%ADda_del_Agua.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/78/Banda_de_Agaete_en_la_Tra%C3%ADda_del_Agua.jpg 2x" data-file-width="320" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Banda_de_Agaete_en_la_Tra%C3%ADda_del_Agua.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Band of <a href="/wiki/Agaete" title="Agaete">Agaete</a> in the <i>Tra\xc3\xadda del Agua</i> (<a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a>).</div></div></div>\n<p>Some holidays of those celebrated in the Canary Islands are international and national, others are regional holidays and others are of insular character. The official day of the autonomous community is <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Canary Islands Day">Canary Islands Day</a> on 30 May. The anniversary of the first session of the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="Parliament of the Canary Islands">Parliament of the Canary Islands</a>, based in the city of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a>, held on 30 May 1983, is commemorated with this day.\n</p><p>The common festive calendar throughout the Canary Islands is as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<center>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align:center;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th width="120">Date\n</th>\n<th width="70">Name\n</th>\n<th width="250">Data\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1 January</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/New_Year" title="New Year">New Year</a></td>\n<td>International festival.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>6 January</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Epiphany_(holiday)" title="Epiphany (holiday)">Epiphany</a></td>\n<td>Catholic festival.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>March or April</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Holy_Thursday" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy Thursday">Holy Thursday</a> and <a href="/wiki/Holy_Friday" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy Friday">Holy Friday</a></td>\n<td>Christian festival.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1 May</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/International_Workers%27_Day" title="International Workers&#39; Day">International Workers\' Day</a></td>\n<td>International festival.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>30 May</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Canary Islands Day">Canary Islands Day</a></td>\n<td>Day of the autonomous community. Anniversary of the first session of the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="Parliament of the Canary Islands">Parliament of the Canary Islands</a>.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>15 August</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Assumption_of_Mary" title="Assumption of Mary">Assumption of Mary</a></td>\n<td>Catholic festival. This day is festive in the archipelago as in all of Spain. Popularly, in the Canary Islands it is known as the day on which the is celebrated of <a href="/wiki/Virgin_of_Candelaria" title="Virgin of Candelaria">Virgin of Candelaria</a> (Saint Patron of the Canary Islands).<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>12 October</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Fiesta_Nacional_de_Espa%C3%B1a" class="mw-redirect" title="Fiesta Nacional de Espa\xc3\xb1a">Fiesta Nacional de Espa\xc3\xb1a</a> (<i>D\xc3\xada de la Hispanidad</i>)</td>\n<td>National Holiday of Spain. Commemoration of <a href="/wiki/Discovery_of_the_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="Discovery of the Americas">discovery of the Americas</a>.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1 November</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/All_Saints%27_Day" title="All Saints&#39; Day">All Saints\' Day</a></td>\n<td>Catholic festival.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>6 December</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Constitution_Day" title="Constitution Day">Constitution Day</a></td>\n<td>Commemoration of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_constitutional_referendum,_1978" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish constitutional referendum, 1978">Spanish constitutional referendum, 1978</a>.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>8 December</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Immaculate_Conception" title="Immaculate Conception">Immaculate Conception</a></td>\n<td>Catholic festival. The Immaculate Conception is the Saint Patron of Spain.\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>25 December</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a></td>\n<td>Christian festival. Commemoration of the birth of <a href="/wiki/Jesus_of_Nazareth" class="mw-redirect" title="Jesus of Nazareth">Jesus of Nazareth</a>.\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</center>\n<p>In addition, each of the islands has an island festival in which it is a holiday only on that island in question. These are the festivities of island patrons saints of each island. Organized chronologically are:<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<center>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" St Mary Major">Our Lady of the Snows</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>8 September</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Virgen_del_Pino" class="new" title="Our Lady of the Pe\xc3\xb1a (page does not exist)">Our Lady of the Pe\xc3\xb1a</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>24 September</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/El_Hierro" title="El Hierro">El Kings</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Monday following the first Saturday of October</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/La_Gomera" title="La Gomera">La Gomera</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Guadalupe" title="Our Lady of Guadalupe">Our Lady of Guadalupe</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</center>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Desfile_del_S%C3%A1bado_de_Carnaval,_en_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Desfile_del_S%C3%A1bado_de_Carnaval%2C_en_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.JPG/330px-Desfile_del_S%C3%A1bado_de_Carnaval%2C_en_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Desfile_del_S%C3%A1bado_de_Carnaval%2C_en_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.JPG/440px-Desfile_del_S%C3%A1bado_de_Carnaval%2C_en_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4896" data-file-height="3672" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Desfile_del_S%C3%A1bado_de_Carnaval,_en_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Parade in the <a href="/wiki/Carnival_of_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Carnival of Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Carnival of Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The most famous festivals of the Canary Islands is the carnival. It is the most famous and international festival of the archipelago. The carnival is celebrated in all the islands and all its municipalities, perhaps the two busiest are those of the two Canarian capitals; the <a href="/wiki/Carnival_of_Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" title="Carnival of Santa Cruz de Tenerife">Carnival of Santa Cruz de Tenerife</a> (<i>Tourist Festival of International Interest</i>) and the <a href="/wiki/Carnival_of_Las_Palmas_de_Gran_Canaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Carnival of Las Palmas de Gran Canaria">Carnival of Las Palmas de Gran Canaria</a>. It is celebrated on the streets between the months of February and March. But the rest of the islands of the archipelago have their carnivals with their own traditions among which stand out: The Festival of the Carneros of <a href="/wiki/El_Hierro" title="El Hierro">El Hierro</a>, the Festival of the Diabletes of <a href="/wiki/Teguise_(municipality)" title="Teguise (municipality)">Teguise</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lanzarote" title="Lanzarote">Lanzarote</a>, Los Indianos de <a href="/wiki/La_Palma" title="La Palma">La Palma</a>, the Carnival of <a href="/wiki/San_Sebasti%C3%A1n_de_La_Gomera" title="San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n de La Gomera">San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n de La Gomera</a> and the Carnival of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_del_Rosario" title="Puerto del Rosario">Puerto del Rosario</a> in <a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura" title="Fuerteventura">Fuerteventura</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Science and technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Erdfunkstelle_Gran_Canaria-3.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Erdfunkstelle_Gran_Canaria-3.JPG/220px-Erdfunkstelle_Gran_Canaria-3.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="91" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Erdfunkstelle_Gran_Canaria-3.JPG/330px-Erdfunkstelle_Gran_Canaria-3.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Erdfunkstelle_Gran_Canaria-3.JPG/440px-Erdfunkstelle_Gran_Canaria-3.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1235" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Erdfunkstelle_Gran_Canaria-3.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gran Canaria space tracking station</div></div></div>\n<p>In the 1960s, Gran Canaria was selected as the location for one of the 14 <a href="/wiki/Ground_stations" class="mw-redirect" title="Ground stations">ground stations</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Manned_Space_Flight_Network" title="Manned Space Flight Network">Manned Space Flight Network</a> (MSFN) to support the <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> space program. <a href="/wiki/Maspalomas_Station" title="Maspalomas Station">Maspalomas Station</a>, located in the south of the island, took part in a number of space missions including the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">Apollo 11</a> Moon landings and <a href="/wiki/Skylab" title="Skylab">Skylab</a>. Today it continues to support satellite communications as part of the <a href="/wiki/ESA" class="mw-redirect" title="ESA">ESA</a> network.<sup id="cite_ref-esa-page_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-esa-page-137">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Because of the remote location, a number of <a href="/wiki/Observatory" title="Observatory">astronomical observatories</a> are located in the archipelago, including the <a href="/wiki/Teide_Observatory" title="Teide Observatory">Teide Observatory</a> on Tenerife, the <a href="/wiki/Roque_de_los_Muchachos_Observatory" title="Roque de los Muchachos Observatory">Roque de los Muchachos Observatory</a> on La Palma, and the <a href="/wiki/Temisas_Astronomical_Observatory" title="Temisas Astronomical Observatory">Temisas Astronomical Observatory</a> on Gran Canaria.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RodriguezLopez2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/RodriguezLopez2008.jpg/220px-RodriguezLopez2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/RodriguezLopez2008.jpg/330px-RodriguezLopez2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/RodriguezLopez2008.jpg/440px-RodriguezLopez2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RodriguezLopez2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Estadio_Heliodoro_Rodr%C3%ADguez_L%C3%B3pez" title="Estadio Heliodoro Rodr\xc3\xadguez L\xc3\xb3pez">Heliodoro Rodr\xc3\xadguez L\xc3\xb3pez Stadium</a> in Tenerife, the stadium with the largest area of field of the Canary Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Estadiogc7septiembre2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Estadiogc7septiembre2008.jpg/220px-Estadiogc7septiembre2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Estadiogc7septiembre2008.jpg/330px-Estadiogc7septiembre2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Estadiogc7septiembre2008.jpg/440px-Estadiogc7septiembre2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Estadiogc7septiembre2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Estadio_Gran_Canaria" title="Estadio Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria Stadium</a>, the biggest sports venue of Canary Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>A unique form of wrestling known as <a href="/wiki/Canarian_wrestling" title="Canarian wrestling">Canarian wrestling</a> (<i>lucha canaria</i>) has opponents stand in a special area called a "terrero" and try to throw each other to the ground using strength and quick movements.<sup id="cite_ref-ctspanish.com_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ctspanish.com-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Another sport is the "game of the sticks" where opponents fence with long sticks. This may have come about from the shepherds of the islands who would challenge each other using their long walking sticks.<sup id="cite_ref-ctspanish.com_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ctspanish.com-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Furthermore, there is the <a href="/wiki/Salto_del_pastor" title="Salto del pastor">shepherd\'s jump</a> (<i>salto del pastor</i>). This involves using a long stick to vault over an open area. This sport possibly evolved from the shepherd\'s need to occasionally get over an open area in the hills as they were tending their sheep.<sup id="cite_ref-ctspanish.com_141-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ctspanish.com-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The two main <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> teams in the archipelago are: the <a href="/wiki/CD_Tenerife" title="CD Tenerife">CD Tenerife</a> (founded in 1912) and <a href="/wiki/UD_Las_Palmas" title="UD Las Palmas">UD Las Palmas</a> (founded in 1949). As of the 2018/2019 season, both Tenerife and Las Palmas play in <a href="/wiki/Liga_Adelante" class="mw-redirect" title="Liga Adelante">Liga Adelante</a>. When in the same division, the clubs contest the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands_derby" title="Canary Islands derby">Canary Islands derby</a>. There are smaller clubs also playing in the mainland <a href="/wiki/Spanish_football_league_system" title="Spanish football league system">Spanish football league system</a>, most notably <a href="/wiki/UD_Lanzarote" title="UD Lanzarote">UD Lanzarote</a> and <a href="/wiki/CD_Laguna_de_Tenerife" title="CD Laguna de Tenerife">CD Laguna</a>, although no other Canarian clubs have played in the top flight.\n</p><p>The mountainous terrain of the Canary Islands also caters to the growing popularity of <a href="/wiki/Ultra_running" class="mw-redirect" title="Ultra running">ultra running</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ultramarathons" class="mw-redirect" title="Ultramarathons">ultramarathons</a> as host of annual competitive long-distance events including <a href="/wiki/CajaMar_Tenerife_Bluetrail" title="CajaMar Tenerife Bluetrail">CajaMar Tenerife Bluetrail</a> on <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transvulcania" title="Transvulcania">Transvulcania</a> on <a href="/wiki/La_Palma" title="La Palma">La Palma</a>, Transgrancanaria<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> on <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria" title="Gran Canaria">Gran Canaria</a>, and the Half <a href="/wiki/Marathon_des_Sables" title="Marathon des Sables">Marathon des Sables</a> on <a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura" title="Fuerteventura">Fuerteventura</a>. A yearly <a href="/wiki/Ironman_Triathlon" title="Ironman Triathlon">Ironman Triathlon</a> has been taking place on <a href="/wiki/Lanzarote" title="Lanzarote">Lanzarote</a> since 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-ironman_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ironman-143">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ironmanhistory_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ironmanhistory-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_athletes">Notable athletes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Canary_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Notable athletes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Paco_Campos" title="Paco Campos">Paco Campos</a>, (1916\xe2\x80\x931995); a footballer who played as a forward. With 127 goals, 120 of which were for <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid" title="Atl\xc3\xa9tico Madrid">Atl\xc3\xa9tico Madrid</a>, he is the highest scoring player from the Canary Islands in <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nicol%C3%A1s_Garc%C3%ADa_(taekwondo)" title="Nicol\xc3\xa1s Garc\xc3\xada (taekwondo)">Nicol\xc3\xa1s Garc\xc3\xada</a> Hemme, born 20 June 1988 in <a href="/wiki/Las_Palmas_de_Gran_Canaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Palmas de Gran Canaria">Las Palmas de Gran Canaria</a>, Canary Islands, <a href="/wiki/2012_London_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="2012 London Olympics">2012 London Olympics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taekwondo" title="Taekwondo">Taekwondo</a> Silver Medalist in Men\'s Welterweight category (\xe2\x88\x9280&#160;kg).</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Al_Cabrera" title="Al Cabrera">Alfredo Cabrera</a>, (1881\xe2\x80\x931964); <a href="/wiki/Shortstop" title="Shortstop">shortstop</a> for the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a> in 1913</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sergio_Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Sergio Rodr\xc3\xadguez">Sergio Rodr\xc3\xadguez</a>, born in <a href="/wiki/San_Crist%C3%B3bal_de_La_Laguna" title="San Crist\xc3\xb3bal de La Laguna">San Crist\xc3\xb3bal de La Laguna</a> in 1986, played <a href="/wiki/Point_guard" title="Point guard">point guard</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Portland_Trail_Blazers" title="Portland Trail Blazers">Portland Trail Blazers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sacramento_Kings" title="Sacramento Kings">Sacramento Kings</a>, and <a href="/wiki/New_York_Knicks" title="New York Knicks">New York Knicks</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/David_Silva" title="David Silva">David Silva</a>, born in <a href="/wiki/Arguinegu%C3%ADn" title="Arguinegu\xc3\xadn">Arguinegu\xc3\xadn</a> in 1986, plays <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> for <a href="/wiki/Real_Sociedad" title="Real Sociedad">Real Sociedad</a>, member of the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 FIFA World Cup</a> champion <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain national football team</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Juan_Carlos_Valer%C3%B3n" title="Juan Carlos Valer\xc3\xb3n">Juan Carlos Valer\xc3\xb3n</a>, born in <a href="/wiki/Arguinegu%C3%ADn" title="Arguinegu\xc3\xadn">Arguinegu\xc3\xadn</a> in 1975, played <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> for <a href="/wiki/Deportivo_de_La_Coru%C3%B1a" title="Deportivo de La Coru\xc3\xb1a">Deportivo la Coruna</a> and <a href="/wiki/UD_Las_Palmas" title="UD Las Palmas">Las Palmas</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pedro_(footballer,_born_1987)" title="Pedro (footballer, born 1987)">Pedro</a>, born in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_de_Tenerife" tennis player</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Paola_Tirados" title="Paola Tirados">Paola Tirados</a>, born in <a href="/wiki/Las_Palmas_de_Gran_Canaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Palmas de Gran Canaria">Las Palmas de Gran Canaria</a> in 1980, synchronized swimmer, who participated in the Olympic Games of 2000, 2004 and 2008. She won the silver medal in Beijing in 2008 in the team competition category.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jes%C3%A9" title="Jes\xc3\xa9">Jes\xc3\xa9</a>, born in <a href="/wiki/Las_Palmas_de_Gran_Canaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Palmas de Gran Canaria">Las Palmas de Gran Canaria</a> in 1993, plays <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> for <a href="/wiki/UD_Las_Palmas" title="UD Las Palmas">Las Palmas</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Christo_Bezuidenhout" title="Christo Bezuidenhout">Christo Bezuidenhout</a>, born in <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a> in 1970, played <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> for <a href="/wiki/Gloucester_Rugby" title="Gloucester Rugby">Gloucester</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_national_rugby_union_team" title="South Africa national rugby union team">South Africa</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pedri" title="Pedri">Pedri</a>, born in <a href="/wiki/Tegueste" title="Tegueste">Tegueste</a> in 2002, plays <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> for <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a>.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
